The World's Composition and the Three Possibilities
Sanusi defines the world and presents the tripartite division for an eternal body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam definition of the world and the three logical possibilities for an eternal body.

Core Idea
Every body must be moving, at rest, or neither—but none works for an eternal body.

Sanusi now moves from rational foundations to the first major proof: the world's temporal origination. He defines the world as everything besides Allah and explains that all bodies are accompanied by accidents like motion and rest. This sets up a tripartite division that will challenge any claim of eternal existence for a body.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the definition of the world and the three cases presented.
Notice the phrase 'لو كان جسم من أجرام العالم... لم يخلُ' which introduces the division.
2
Understand the definition of the world
Sanusi defines the world as everything other than Allah, and says it consists of bodies (ajram) to which accidents (a'rad) like motion and rest inhere.
This definition is crucial for the proof.
3
Identify the three possibilities
The passage presents three possibilities for an eternal body: moving, at rest, or neither moving nor at rest. Note that these are presented as exhaustive.
The impossibility of all three will prove temporal origination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا عرفت هذا : فأَوَّلُ ما تبدأُ بِهِ مِنَ النظرِ : النظرُ في حدوثِ العالم ؛ وهو كلُّ ما سوى الله تبارك وتعالى ، فإذا نظرت فيه تجد جميعَهُ أجراماً تقوم بها أعراض ؛ مِنْ حركة وسكون وغيرهما ، فتقول في برهان حدوثِهِ : لو كان جسم من أجرامِ العالَمِ كالسماء والأرض مثلاً موجوداً في الأزل .. لم يخلُ : إما أن يكون في الأزلِ مُتحرِّكاً ، أو ساكناً ، أو لا متحركاً ولا ساكناً ، والأقسام الثلاثة مستحيلة على الجِرْمِ في الأزلِ ؛ فيكون وجود الجزم في الأزلِ مستحيلاً ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُعقَلُ وجوده عارياً عن تلك الأقسام الثلاثة . أمَّا بيانُ استحالةِ القسم الثالث : فظاهر ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُعقَلُ جرم في الأزلِ ولا فيما لا يزالُ .. ليس ثابتاً في الحيّز ولا منتقلاً عنه . وأما بيان استحالة القسم الثاني - وهو كونُ الجِرْم ساكناً في الأزلِ - فوجهُهُ : أَنَّهُ لو كان كذلكَ لَمَا قَبِلَ أَنْ يتحرَّكَ
And if you have known this, then the first thing you begin with in examination is the examination of the temporal origination of the world; and it is everything other than Allah, Blessed and Exalted. So if you examine it, you find all of it to be bodies (ajram) to which accidents (a'rad) inhere, such as movement, rest, and others. So you say in the proof of its temporal origination: if a body (jism) among the bodies of the world, like the sky and the earth for example, existed in pre-eternity (al-azal), it would not be free from [one of three cases]: either it would be in pre-eternity moving, or at rest, or neither moving nor at rest. And the three divisions are impossible for the body in pre-eternity. Thus, the existence of a body in pre-eternity is impossible, because its existence bare of those three divisions is not conceivable. As for the explanation of the impossibility of the third division: it is apparent, because a body in pre-eternity and in perpetuity (ma la yazalu) cannot be conceived as not fixed in a locus (al-hayyiz) nor as moving from it. And as for the explanation of the impossibility of the second division—which is the body being at rest in pre-eternity—its aspect is that if it were like that, it would not be able to become moving.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents the classical kalam argument (burhan al-tamānu‘ or similar) for the temporal origination of the world. The author first establishes that the world (al-‘ālam) is everything other than Allah, and it consists of bodies (ajrām) that are necessarily accompanied by accidents (a‘rād) such as motion and rest.

The argument proceeds as follows:
- Suppose a particular body (e.g., the sky or the earth) were eternal (existed in pre-eternity, al-azal).
- That eternal body would have to be either: (1) moving, (2) at rest, or (3) neither moving nor at rest. These are the only possibilities.
- Sanusi argues that all three are impossible for an eternal body:
   - The third case (neither moving nor at rest) is clearly impossible because a body must either be in a particular place (fixed) or moving from it; such a neutral state is inconceivable for a body.
   - The second case (eternally at rest) is also impossible, because if it were eternally at rest, it would be incapable of ever becoming moving (change from rest to motion would be impossible).
- The first case (eternally moving) is not explicitly discussed here, but the implication is that it too is impossible because motion is an accident that cannot be eternal (as per other kalam arguments).
- Therefore, since all three options are impossible, no body can be eternal. Hence, the world (composed of bodies) must have a temporal beginning (ḥudūth).

The passage ends mid-sentence with the start of the explanation for the second case. The complete argument would also refute eternal motion, but the provided text stops here. The proof relies on the principle that bodies cannot exist without accidents, and accidents are temporal, so bodies must be temporal.

Key Terms
حدوث العالم
الأزل
الجسم
العرض
الحركة
السكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the world includes Allah or that the proof aims to prove Allah's existence directly.
Correction: The world is defined as everything other than Allah, and the proof shows the world is temporally originated, which then leads to the need for a Creator, but does not directly prove Him.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three logical possibilities for an eternal body?
A) Moving, at rest, or neither
B) Hot, cold, or moderate
C) Created, uncreated, or both
D) In space, out of space, or both

Key Takeaway
The kalam proof for the world's temporal origination begins by defining the world and showing that an eternal body would have to be in one of three impossible states.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every body you see – the sky, the earth, your own body – had a beginning, then nothing in the universe can claim eternity for itself. What does that mean for your attachment to created things? Are you holding on to something as if it will last forever?
?
The proof shows that an eternal body is inconceivable. You know that only Allah is eternal. Have you ever acted as if something in this world is permanent – like your health, your wealth, or your relationships? How does this lesson change your perspective on that thing today?
?
You exist because Allah willed you into being at a specific moment. If you truly believe that, what claim does He have over your life? Are you living as if you owe Him everything, or as if you are self-made?

Impossibility of the Third and Second Divisions
Sanusi explains the impossibility of the third division (neither moving nor rest) and begins explaining the impossibility of the second (eternal rest).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an eternal body cannot be neither moving nor at rest, and why it cannot be eternally at rest.

Core Idea
An eternal body cannot be neither moving nor at rest, and if eternally at rest it could never move.

Having established that an eternal body must be either moving, at rest, or neither, Sanusi now refutes two of these possibilities. He first shows that 'neither moving nor at rest' is inconceivable for any body. Then he begins to explain why eternal rest is also impossible, because it would prevent the body from ever acquiring motion. This completes the proof that bodies cannot be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of the third division
Focus on why a body cannot be neither moving nor at rest in pre-eternity. Sanusi says it is 'apparent' because a body must either be fixed in a place or moving from it.
Think about what it means for a body to 'exist' spatially.
2
Read the start of the explanation for the second division
Sanusi argues that if a body were eternally at rest, it would never be able to become moving. This is because a change from eternal rest to motion would require a cause, but the eternal state would be immutable.
The argument assumes that an eternal attribute cannot change.
3
Connect to the overall proof
Realize that these refutations, together with the refutation of eternal motion (not in this passage), show that no body can be eternal, thus the world is temporally originated.
This lesson covers the third and part of the second division; the first division will be handled separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا عرفت هذا : فأَوَّلُ ما تبدأُ بِهِ مِنَ النظرِ : النظرُ في حدوثِ العالم ؛ وهو كلُّ ما سوى الله تبارك وتعالى ، فإذا نظرت فيه تجد جميعَهُ أجراماً تقوم بها أعراض ؛ مِنْ حركة وسكون وغيرهما ، فتقول في برهان حدوثِهِ : لو كان جسم من أجرامِ العالَمِ كالسماء والأرض مثلاً موجوداً في الأزل .. لم يخلُ : إما أن يكون في الأزلِ مُتحرِّكاً ، أو ساكناً ، أو لا متحركاً ولا ساكناً ، والأقسام الثلاثة مستحيلة على الجِرْمِ في الأزلِ ؛ فيكون وجود الجزم في الأزلِ مستحيلاً ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُعقَلُ وجوده عارياً عن تلك الأقسام الثلاثة . أمَّا بيانُ استحالةِ القسم الثالث : فظاهر ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُعقَلُ جرم في الأزلِ ولا فيما لا يزالُ .. ليس ثابتاً في الحيّز ولا منتقلاً عنه . وأما بيان استحالة القسم الثاني - وهو كونُ الجِرْم ساكناً في الأزلِ - فوجهُهُ : أَنَّهُ لو كان كذلكَ لَمَا قَبِلَ أَنْ يتحرَّكَ
And if you have known this, then the first thing you begin with in examination is the examination of the temporal origination of the world; and it is everything other than Allah, Blessed and Exalted. So if you examine it, you find all of it to be bodies (ajram) to which accidents (a'rad) inhere, such as movement, rest, and others. So you say in the proof of its temporal origination: if a body (jism) among the bodies of the world, like the sky and the earth for example, existed in pre-eternity (al-azal), it would not be free from [one of three cases]: either it would be in pre-eternity moving, or at rest, or neither moving nor at rest. And the three divisions are impossible for the body in pre-eternity. Thus, the existence of a body in pre-eternity is impossible, because its existence bare of those three divisions is not conceivable. As for the explanation of the impossibility of the third division: it is apparent, because a body in pre-eternity and in perpetuity (ma la yazalu) cannot be conceived as not fixed in a locus (al-hayyiz) nor as moving from it. And as for the explanation of the impossibility of the second division—which is the body being at rest in pre-eternity—its aspect is that if it were like that, it would not be able to become moving.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents the classical kalam argument (burhan al-tamānu‘ or similar) for the temporal origination of the world. The author first establishes that the world (al-‘ālam) is everything other than Allah, and it consists of bodies (ajrām) that are necessarily accompanied by accidents (a‘rād) such as motion and rest.

The argument proceeds as follows:
- Suppose a particular body (e.g., the sky or the earth) were eternal (existed in pre-eternity, al-azal).
- That eternal body would have to be either: (1) moving, (2) at rest, or (3) neither moving nor at rest. These are the only possibilities.
- Sanusi argues that all three are impossible for an eternal body:
   - The third case (neither moving nor at rest) is clearly impossible because a body must either be in a particular place (fixed) or moving from it; such a neutral state is inconceivable for a body.
   - The second case (eternally at rest) is also impossible, because if it were eternally at rest, it would be incapable of ever becoming moving (change from rest to motion would be impossible).
- The first case (eternally moving) is not explicitly discussed here, but the implication is that it too is impossible because motion is an accident that cannot be eternal (as per other kalam arguments).
- Therefore, since all three options are impossible, no body can be eternal. Hence, the world (composed of bodies) must have a temporal beginning (ḥudūth).

The passage ends mid-sentence with the start of the explanation for the second case. The complete argument would also refute eternal motion, but the provided text stops here. The proof relies on the principle that bodies cannot exist without accidents, and accidents are temporal, so bodies must be temporal.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'neither moving nor at rest' is a valid state for immaterial beings, but here we are discussing bodies (ajram) which are physical.
Correction: The argument is about bodies, which are spatial entities. For them, the third division is indeed impossible.

Checkpoint
Why is the third division (neither moving nor at rest) impossible for a body in pre-eternity?
A) Because motion and rest are the only two accidents that a body can have
B) Because a body must be either fixed in a place or moving from it
C) Because the body would be non-existent
D) Because it would require a cause that cannot exist in pre-eternity

Key Takeaway
An eternal body cannot be in a state of neither motion nor rest, nor can it be eternally at rest—both are contradictory to the nature of bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If an eternal body cannot be at rest without being trapped in a state from which it can never change, what does that say about your own spiritual state if you have grown comfortable and stagnant in your practice? Are you at risk of being unable to move toward Allah? What concrete step will you take today to break a pattern of spiritual rest?
?
The third division—neither moving nor rest—is logically impossible for any body. In your own life, can you identify an area where you are 'neither here nor there'—neither committing to obedience nor fully at rest in disobedience? How can you abandon this impossible state and take a definite position?
?
Sanusi argues that an eternally resting body cannot later move. If you find yourself at rest in a sin or a bad habit, what cause do you think will ever move you out of it if you do not actively seek a change now? Will you wait for a miracle, or will you invoke Allah's help and act?

Allah's Existence

Proof of Creation: The Impossibility of Eternal Rest
Sanusi presents the second case impossibility for an eternal body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the possibility of a body being eternally at rest, and why this refutation is key to proving the world's origination.

Core Idea
An eternal body at rest could never begin to move, proving it cannot be eternal.

In this lesson, we begin Sanusi's proof for the creation of the world. He first establishes that every worldly thing is a body with accidents. He then argues that if any body existed eternally, it must be either moving, at rest, or neither. He quickly dismisses the third option, then focuses on the second: eternal rest. Through a careful argument, he shows that an eternally resting body would be impossible because it could never start moving, contradicting our observation that motion does occur.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three cases
Read the Arabic passage once through. Notice how Sanusi lists three possible states for an eternal body: moving, resting, or neither. Then read the translation to ensure understanding.
The three cases are exhaustive – no other states are possible for a body.
2
Focus on the second case: eternal rest
The second case is that the body is eternally at rest. Sanusi argues that if it were eternally at rest, it could never move; because the eternal cannot cease to exist. But we observe motion, so rest cannot be eternal.
This argument uses the principle that what is eternal cannot admit of non-existence.
3
Understand the role of similarity (tamāthul)
Sanusi claims that because we observe motion in some bodies, and all bodies are similar in nature, motion is possible for every body. This refutes the assumption that any body is eternally at rest.
The similarity of bodies is taken as evident – all bodies share the same essence with respect to motion and rest.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
After showing the impossibility of the second case, reflect on how this fits into the overall proof: if a body cannot be eternally at rest, it cannot be eternal. We still have to consider the first case (eternal motion) in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في حدوث العالم، وإقامة البرهان القاطع عليه. فإذا عرفت هذا: فأول ما تبدأ به من النظر: النظر في حدوث العالم؛ وهو كل ما سوى الله تبارك وتعالى، فإذا نظرت فيه تجد جميعه أجراماً تقوم بها أعراض؛ من حركة وسكون وغيرهما، فتقول في برهان حدوثه: لو كان جرم من أجرام العالم كالسماء والأرض مثلاً موجوداً في الأزل .. لم يخل: إما أن يكون في الأزل متحركاً، أو ساكناً، أو لا متحركاً ولا ساكناً، والأقسام الثلاثة مستحيلة على الجرم في الأزل؛ فيكون وجود الجرم في الأزل مستحيلاً؛ لأنه لا يعقل وجوده عارياً عن تلك الأقسام الثلاثة.

أما بيان استحالة القسم الثالث: فظاهر؛ لأنه لا يعقل جرم في الأزل ولا فيما لا يزال .. ليس ثابتاً في الحيز ولا منتقلاً عنه.

وأما بيان استحالة القسم الثاني - وهو كون الجرم ساكناً في الأزل - فوجهه: أنه لو كان كذلك لما قبل أن يتحرك أبداً؛ لأن سكونه على هذا الفرض قديم، والقديم لا يقبل العدم؛ إذ لو قبل العدم لاحتاج وجوده إلى مخصص؛ لجوازه حينئذ، فيكون محدثاً، وقد فرض قديماً، فهذا تناقض لا يعقل، ودليل قبول السكون العدم: مشاهدتنا الحركة في بعض الأجرام، وذلك يقضي بجواز الحركة على جميع الأجرام؛ لتماثلها.

وأما بيان استحالة القسم الأول - وهو كون الجرم في الأزل متحركاً - فالوجه فيه: ما عرفت الآن في استحالة القسم الثاني، ويزيد هذا القسم بوجه آخر من الاستحالة؛ أن حقيقة الحركة لا تعقل قديمة؛ إذ هي الانتقال من حيز إلى حيز، فهي إذاً لا تكون إلا طارئة على الجرم، ولا بد أن يتقدم على وجودها الكون في الحيز المنتقل عنه، والقديم لا يتصور أن يكون طارئاً، ولا أن يتقدم على وجوده غيره.

فقد خرج لك بهذا البرهان القطعي: كون العالم كله حادثاً؛ من عرشه إلى فرشه، لا يتصور في العقل أن يكون شيء منه قديماً.
Chapter on the origination of the world and establishing the conclusive proof upon it. Since you have known this: the first thing you begin with from investigation is the investigation into the origination of the world; and it is everything other than God, Blessed and Most High. So if you investigate it, you find all of it to be bodies (ajrām) to which accidents (a‘rāḍ) inhere, of motion (ḥarakah), rest (sukūn), and others. So you say in the proof of its origination: If a body (jirm) from the bodies of the world, like the heaven and the earth for example, existed in pre-eternity (al-azal) ... it cannot be free: either it is in pre-eternity moving, or resting, or neither moving nor resting. And the three divisions are impossible for the body in pre-eternity; thus the existence of the body in pre-eternity is impossible; because its existence stripped of those three divisions cannot be conceived.

As for the explanation of the impossibility of the third division: it is obvious; because a body cannot be conceived in pre-eternity nor in what never ceases ... not fixed in a place nor moving from it.

As for the explanation of the impossibility of the second division – namely the body being at rest in pre-eternity – its aspect is: that if it were so, it would never accept that it could move at all; because its rest on this assumption is eternal (qadīm), and the eternal does not accept non-existence; because if it accepted non-existence, its existence would need a specific (mukhaṣṣiṣ) on account of its contingency then, so it would be originated (muḥdath), and it was assumed eternal, so this is an inconceivable contradiction. And the evidence that rest accepts non-existence is our observation of motion in some bodies, and that necessitates the possibility of motion upon all bodies, due to their similarity (tamāthulihā).

As for the explanation of the impossibility of the first division – namely the body being in motion in pre-eternity – its aspect is that which you have now understood regarding the impossibility of the second division, and this division is increased by another aspect of impossibility: that the reality of motion cannot be conceived as eternal; because it is the transfer from one place to another, so it is thus only accidental (ṭāri’ah) upon the body, and it is necessary that its existence be preceded by the being in the place from which it transfers. And the eternal cannot be conceived as accidental, nor can anything else precede its existence.

So there has come out for you by this conclusive proof: that the entire world is originated; from its Throne to its carpet; it cannot be conceived in the mind that any part of it is eternal.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (burhān) for the origination (ḥudūth) of the world. It is a classification of possible states for an eternal body leading to impossibility. The author begins by defining the world as everything other than God and stating that all worldly things are bodies (ajrām) possessing accidents (a‘rāḍ) like motion and rest. The proof then proceeds as a reductio ad absurdum: assume some body (e.g., the sky or earth) existed in pre-eternity (al-azal). Such a body cannot be devoid of three possibilities: it is either moving, at rest, or neither. The author then argues each case is impossible. The third case (neither moving nor at rest) is dismissed as inconceivable: a body must either be fixed in a place or moving from it. The second case (eternal rest) is impossible because if the body had always been at rest, it could never begin to move; the eternal (qadīm) cannot cease to be (lā yaqbal al-‘adam). If it were possible for it to cease, then its existence would require a specific cause (mukhaṣṣiṣ), making it originated (muḥdath), contradicting its assumed eternity. Moreover, we observe motion in some bodies, and all bodies are similar (tamāthul), so motion is possible for any body; thus the assumption of eternal rest is invalid. The first case (eternal motion) is impossible for the same reason (if eternal, it could never cease; but motion is observed to cease), plus an additional argument: motion is essentially a transition, which is accidental (ṭāri’) and requires a prior state (the body’s being in the starting place). The eternal cannot be accidental or preceded by anything. Therefore, no body can be eternal; hence the entire world—from the Throne to the carpet—is originated. The proof is presented as conclusive (qaṭ‘ī).

Key Terms
ḥudūth
qadīm
jirm
sukūn
azal
tamāthul

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof assumes all bodies are identical in every aspect, but Sanusi only asserts similarity in their nature as bodies, which is enough to extend the possibility of motion.
Correction: The term tamāthul (similarity) refers to the shared essential property of being a body (jismiyah), not accidental similarities. Since all bodies share the same category, what is possible for one is possible for another.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi argue that a body cannot be eternally at rest?
A) Because rest is not a real accident.
B) Because if it were eternally at rest, it could never begin to move, contradicting the observation of motion.
C) Because bodies are naturally moving.
D) Because the Quran states the world is created.

Key Takeaway
An eternal body at rest is impossible because the eternal cannot cease to be, but rest is observed to cease, so the body cannot be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that nothing in the created world can be eternal—it must have a beginning. When you look at the world around you, what created things do you tend to act as if they are permanent (e.g., your health, your routines, your relationships)? How does this logical truth challenge you to re-evaluate your attachment to them? Will you take one concrete step today to loosen your grip on something you treat as if it will never end?
?
You have seen change and motion in your own life—your body changes, your circumstances shift. The proof says that if something is truly eternal, it cannot change. Does the certainty that only Allah is unchanging bring you comfort or anxiety? Will you consciously remind yourself of His permanence the next time you feel threatened by change? What will you tell yourself?
?
The argument uses the similarity of all bodies to show that motion is possible for any body. But what about your own soul? If everything in the world is originated and contingent, then your own existence is a gift sustained moment by moment. How does this realization affect the way you start your day—do you begin with gratitude and reliance on the Creator? If not, what will you change tomorrow morning?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
5 min
The Impossibility of Eternal Motion and the Conclusion
Sanusi refutes the first case (eternal motion) and concludes the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why eternal motion is impossible for a body and how the entire proof establishes that the world is originated.

Core Idea
Eternal motion is impossible because motion is an accident that must be preceded by a state.

In this lesson, we complete Sanusi's proof by examining the first case: that a body could be eternally in motion. Sanusi argues that motion is essentially a transition from one place to another, which implies it is accidental and preceded by a prior state. The eternal cannot be accidental or preceded. Therefore, the first case is impossible as well. This leaves no possibility for any body to be eternal, concluding that the entire world—from Throne to carpet—is originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the first case
Read the Arabic passage for the impossibility of eternal motion. Note the additional argument beyond that used for rest: motion is a transition, thus accidental.
Motion is defined as transition (intiqāl) from one place to another.
2
Compare with the second case argument
The first case shares the same general argument as the second (the eternal cannot cease), but adds a unique point: motion is inherently accidental (ṭāri’) and cannot be eternal because it requires a prior state.
The eternal cannot be accidental because accidents are contingent upon their subjects.
3
Understand the final conclusion
After all three cases are shown impossible, the proof concludes that no body can be eternal. Therefore, the entire world, every part, is originated.
The phrase 'from its Throne to its carpet' emphasizes that nothing in creation is eternal.
4
Reflect on the proof as a whole
Consider the strength of this reductio ad absurdum argument. It covers all possibilities and uses only rational reasoning without relying on scripture.
This proof is considered conclusive (qaṭ‘ī) in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في حدوث العالم، وإقامة البرهان القاطع عليه. فإذا عرفت هذا: فأول ما تبدأ به من النظر: النظر في حدوث العالم؛ وهو كل ما سوى الله تبارك وتعالى، فإذا نظرت فيه تجد جميعه أجراماً تقوم بها أعراض؛ من حركة وسكون وغيرهما، فتقول في برهان حدوثه: لو كان جرم من أجرام العالم كالسماء والأرض مثلاً موجوداً في الأزل .. لم يخل: إما أن يكون في الأزل متحركاً، أو ساكناً، أو لا متحركاً ولا ساكناً، والأقسام الثلاثة مستحيلة على الجرم في الأزل؛ فيكون وجود الجرم في الأزل مستحيلاً؛ لأنه لا يعقل وجوده عارياً عن تلك الأقسام الثلاثة.

أما بيان استحالة القسم الثالث: فظاهر؛ لأنه لا يعقل جرم في الأزل ولا فيما لا يزال .. ليس ثابتاً في الحيز ولا منتقلاً عنه.

وأما بيان استحالة القسم الثاني - وهو كون الجرم ساكناً في الأزل - فوجهه: أنه لو كان كذلك لما قبل أن يتحرك أبداً؛ لأن سكونه على هذا الفرض قديم، والقديم لا يقبل العدم؛ إذ لو قبل العدم لاحتاج وجوده إلى مخصص؛ لجوازه حينئذ، فيكون محدثاً، وقد فرض قديماً، فهذا تناقض لا يعقل، ودليل قبول السكون العدم: مشاهدتنا الحركة في بعض الأجرام، وذلك يقضي بجواز الحركة على جميع الأجرام؛ لتماثلها.

وأما بيان استحالة القسم الأول - وهو كون الجرم في الأزل متحركاً - فالوجه فيه: ما عرفت الآن في استحالة القسم الثاني، ويزيد هذا القسم بوجه آخر من الاستحالة؛ أن حقيقة الحركة لا تعقل قديمة؛ إذ هي الانتقال من حيز إلى حيز، فهي إذاً لا تكون إلا طارئة على الجرم، ولا بد أن يتقدم على وجودها الكون في الحيز المنتقل عنه، والقديم لا يتصور أن يكون طارئاً، ولا أن يتقدم على وجوده غيره.

فقد خرج لك بهذا البرهان القطعي: كون العالم كله حادثاً؛ من عرشه إلى فرشه، لا يتصور في العقل أن يكون شيء منه قديماً.
Chapter on the origination of the world and establishing the conclusive proof upon it. Since you have known this: the first thing you begin with from investigation is the investigation into the origination of the world; and it is everything other than God, Blessed and Most High. So if you investigate it, you find all of it to be bodies (ajrām) to which accidents (a‘rāḍ) inhere, of motion (ḥarakah), rest (sukūn), and others. So you say in the proof of its origination: If a body (jirm) from the bodies of the world, like the heaven and the earth for example, existed in pre-eternity (al-azal) ... it cannot be free: either it is in pre-eternity moving, or resting, or neither moving nor resting. And the three divisions are impossible for the body in pre-eternity; thus the existence of the body in pre-eternity is impossible; because its existence stripped of those three divisions cannot be conceived.

As for the explanation of the impossibility of the third division: it is obvious; because a body cannot be conceived in pre-eternity nor in what never ceases ... not fixed in a place nor moving from it.

As for the explanation of the impossibility of the second division – namely the body being at rest in pre-eternity – its aspect is: that if it were so, it would never accept that it could move at all; because its rest on this assumption is eternal (qadīm), and the eternal does not accept non-existence; because if it accepted non-existence, its existence would need a specific (mukhaṣṣiṣ) on account of its contingency then, so it would be originated (muḥdath), and it was assumed eternal, so this is an inconceivable contradiction. And the evidence that rest accepts non-existence is our observation of motion in some bodies, and that necessitates the possibility of motion upon all bodies, due to their similarity (tamāthulihā).

As for the explanation of the impossibility of the first division – namely the body being in motion in pre-eternity – its aspect is that which you have now understood regarding the impossibility of the second division, and this division is increased by another aspect of impossibility: that the reality of motion cannot be conceived as eternal; because it is the transfer from one place to another, so it is thus only accidental (ṭāri’ah) upon the body, and it is necessary that its existence be preceded by the being in the place from which it transfers. And the eternal cannot be conceived as accidental, nor can anything else precede its existence.

So there has come out for you by this conclusive proof: that the entire world is originated; from its Throne to its carpet; it cannot be conceived in the mind that any part of it is eternal.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (burhān) for the origination (ḥudūth) of the world. It is a classification of possible states for an eternal body leading to impossibility. The author begins by defining the world as everything other than God and stating that all worldly things are bodies (ajrām) possessing accidents (a‘rāḍ) like motion and rest. The proof then proceeds as a reductio ad absurdum: assume some body (e.g., the sky or earth) existed in pre-eternity (al-azal). Such a body cannot be devoid of three possibilities: it is either moving, at rest, or neither. The author then argues each case is impossible. The third case (neither moving nor at rest) is dismissed as inconceivable: a body must either be fixed in a place or moving from it. The second case (eternal rest) is impossible because if the body had always been at rest, it could never begin to move; the eternal (qadīm) cannot cease to be (lā yaqbal al-‘adam). If it were possible for it to cease, then its existence would require a specific cause (mukhaṣṣiṣ), making it originated (muḥdath), contradicting its assumed eternity. Moreover, we observe motion in some bodies, and all bodies are similar (tamāthul), so motion is possible for any body; thus the assumption of eternal rest is invalid. The first case (eternal motion) is impossible for the same reason (if eternal, it could never cease; but motion is observed to cease), plus an additional argument: motion is essentially a transition, which is accidental (ṭāri’) and requires a prior state (the body’s being in the starting place). The eternal cannot be accidental or preceded by anything. Therefore, no body can be eternal; hence the entire world—from the Throne to the carpet—is originated. The proof is presented as conclusive (qaṭ‘ī).

Key Terms
ḥarakah
ṭāri’
intiqāl
azal
muḥdath

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key additional reason Sanusi gives for the impossibility of eternal motion?
A) Motion requires a mover.
B) Motion is a transfer, making it an accident that cannot be eternal.
C) Bodies are too heavy to move eternally.
D) The Quran states that everything moves.

Key Takeaway
Eternal motion is impossible because motion is an accidental transition, and the eternal cannot be accidental. Thus, the entire world is originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything from the Throne to the carpet is originated, including your own existence, what does that demand of you right now in terms of your relationship with the Eternal Creator?
?
When you consider that your very plans, ambitions, and the things you depend on are all originated and cannot be eternal, does that shift where you place your ultimate trust? Will you concretely surrender something temporal today to anchor yourself in the Eternal?
?
The proof shows that even motion cannot be eternal; your own actions and movements are contingent. Does knowing that your entire existence is a series of originated accidents humble you enough to submit every moment to the One who alone is not an accident?

The Decisive Proof for the World's Origination
Sanusi refutes eternal rest and motion to prove the world's origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the decisive proof (burhān qaṭ‘ī) for the origination of the entire world by demonstrating the impossibility of eternal rest and eternal motion.

Core Idea
Neither eternal rest nor eternal motion can be rationally conceived.

Sanusi now presents a rigorous proof that the entire world is originated. He considers two logical possibilities for the world existing eternally: either it is in a state of rest or motion. By showing that both are impossible, he establishes that the world must have a beginning. This proof is foundational for establishing the existence of a Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the English translation. Notice how Sanusi builds his argument step by step.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the argument against eternal rest
Sanusi first shows that if the world were in a state of eternal rest, that rest would have to be eternal. But the eternal cannot accept non-existence. However, we observe motion in bodies, proving that rest can cease. Therefore eternal rest is impossible.
3
Understand the argument against eternal motion
Next, he shows that eternal motion is also impossible because motion is accidental (it comes and goes) and requires a prior state of being in a starting location. The eternal cannot be accidental or preceded by anything.
This second argument strengthens the proof.
4
Grasp the conclusion
With both possibilities eliminated, the only rational conclusion is that the entire world from the Throne to the Footstool is originated. Nothing within creation can be eternal.
This is a 'decisive proof' (burhān qaṭ‘ī).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبداً؛ لأنَّ سكونَهُ على هذا الفَرْضِ قديم ، والقديم لا يقبلُ العدمَ ؛ إذ لو قبل العدم لاحتاج وجوده إلى مُخصص ؛ لجوازه حينئذ ، فيكونُ مُحْدَثاً ، وقد فُرِضَ قديماً ، فهذا تناقض لا يُعقَلُ ، ودليل قبول السكون العدم : مشاهدتُنا الحركة في بعض الأجرام ، وذلك يقضي بجواز الحركة على جميع الأجرام ؛ لتماثلها • وأما بيانُ استحالة القسم الأول ـ وهو كونُ الجِرْمِ في الأزلِ مُتحرِّكاً - فالوجه فيه : ما عرفت الآن في استحالة القسم الثاني ، ويزيدُ هذا القسم بوجه آخرَ مِنَ الاستحالة ؛ أنَّ حقيقة الحركةِ لا تُعقَلُ قديمةً ؛ إذْ هي الانتقالُ مِنْ حيز إلى حيز ، فهي إذاً لا تكون إلا طارئةً على الجِرْمِ ، ولا بدَّ أنْ يتقدَّمَ على وجودِها الكونُ في الحيز المنتقل عنه ، والقديم لا يُتصوَّرُ أنْ يكونَ طارئاً ، ولا أنْ يتقدَّمَ على وجودِهِ غیره . فقد خرج لك بهذا البرهان القطعي : كونُ العالَمِ كَلَّهِ حادثاً ؛ مِنْ عرشِهِ إِلى فَرْشِهِ ، لا يُتصوَّرُ في العقلِ أنْ يكونَ شيء منه قديماً
Forever; because its rest on this assumption is eternal, and the eternal does not accept non-existence; if it accepted non-existence, its existence would need a particularizer due to its possibility then, so it would be originated, while it was assumed eternal, so this is a contradiction not rationally conceivable. And the evidence for the acceptance of non-existence by rest: our observation of motion in some bodies, which necessitates the possibility of motion in all bodies due to their similarity. As for the clarification of the impossibility of the first division – that the body is in eternity moving – the aspect in it is what you have now known regarding the impossibility of the second division, and this division is increased by another aspect of impossibility: that the reality of motion is not conceivable as eternal; since it is transition from one location to another, so it is only accidental to the body, and there must precede its existence the being in the location from which it transitions, and the eternal cannot be conceived as accidental, nor that something else precedes its existence. So by this decisive proof it has come out for you: that the entire world is originated, from its Throne to its Footstool, not conceivable in reason that anything from it is eternal.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the origination (ḥudūth) of the entire world. The author first refutes the possibility of the world being in a state of eternal rest (sukūn qadīm). If rest were eternal, it could not accept non-existence; if it could, that would prove it originated (ḥādith), contradicting the assumption. But we observe motion, which shows rest can cease, so eternal rest is impossible. Then he refutes eternal motion (ḥaraka qadīma) because motion is accidental (ṭāriʼ) and must be preceded by the body being in the starting location; the eternal cannot be accidental nor preceded. Therefore, the world must be originated, from the Throne to the Footstool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The world could be eternal if it were in a state of unchanging rest.
Correction: Eternal rest is impossible because rest can cease—as proven by the existence of motion—and what can cease cannot be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The entire world, from the Throne to the Footstool, is originated; nothing within it can be rationally conceived as eternal.

Proof of God's Existence from the Origination of the World
Sanusi argues for a Creator from the origination of the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalām argument that the originated world must have a Creator, and why the emergence of existence from non-existence requires a free agent.

Core Idea
The world's transition from non-existence to existence demands a Creator.

This lesson presents the classical proof of God's existence based on the origination (ḥudūth) of the world. Sanusi argues that since the world was preceded by non-existence, it cannot bring itself into being; it requires an originator. He then addresses a key objection about the equality of existence and non-existence, showing that non-existence is more original, making existence an outweighed state that cannot arise without a cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical flow and key terms.
Pay attention to the terms 'محدث' (originator) and 'فاعل مختار' (free agent).
2
Identify the core argument
The passage argues: the world is originated (it was preceded by non-existence). For it to come into existence, it must have an originator, because a thing cannot bring itself from non-existence to existence without a cause.
This is a deductive proof: if A then B, and A is true, so B.
3
Understand the objection and response
Sanusi discusses that existence and non-existence are either equal relative to the world, or non-existence is more appropriate. In either case, existence is either equal or outweighed. Since preponderance of an equal or outweigh without a cause is impossible, a cause must exist.
The cause is the Creator (Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في إقامة البرهان القاطع على وجوده تعالى و بيان احتیاج العالم اليه جل وعز. وإذا كانَ العالم حادثاً بعدما تقرَّرَ عدمُهُ . . فلا بدَّ لَهُ مِنْ محدث ؛ إذْ لا يُتصوَّرُ في العقل انتقالُهُ مِنَ العدم الذي كانَ عليه إلى الوجودِ الطارئ بلا سبب ، ولولا الفاعل المختارُ لوجوده فيما شاءَ مِنَ الأزمانِ على ما شاءَ مِنَ المقادير والصفاتِ .. لكان يجب أن يبقى على ما كانَ عليهِ مِنَ العدمِ أبد الآبادِ ؛ لاستواء المقادير والصفاتِ والأزمانِ بالنسبة إلى ذاته . وأما الوجود والعدم : فقيل : هما بالنسبة إلى ذاتِهِ سواءٌ ، فيستحيل أن يتربَّحَ الوجود المساوي الطارئ بلا سببٍ ، وقيل : العدمُ السابق أولى به ؛ لأصالته فيه ، وعدم افتقارِهِ إلى سببٍ ، وإذا كان ترجيح أحد المتساويين بلا سبب محالاً . فاستحالة ترجیح الوجود المرجوح بالنسبة إلى العالم على هذا بلا سبب أحرى
Chapter: On establishing the decisive proof for His existence, may He be exalted, and explaining the world's need for Him, glorified and exalted. And when the world is originated after its non-existence was established... then it must have an originator; for it is not rationally conceivable for it to transition from the non-existence it was upon to accidental existence without a cause. And were it not for the free agent bringing it into existence whenever He wills from times, with whatever measures and attributes He wills, it would necessarily remain upon what it was upon of non-existence forever; because measures, attributes, and times are equal relative to its essence. And as for existence and non-existence: it is said: they are equal relative to its essence, so it is impossible for equal existence to preponderate without a cause. And it is said: the prior non-existence is more appropriate for it due to its originality in it and its lack of need for a cause. And if preponderance of one of two equals without a cause is impossible, then preponderance of the outweighed existence relative to the world without a cause is even more impossible.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage establishes the proof of God's existence based on the origination (ḥudūth) of the world. Since the world is originated, it must have an originator (muḥdith) because it cannot move from non-existence to existence without a cause. Without a free agent (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār) choosing its time, measure, and attributes, the world would have remained in non-existence forever. The author then discusses an objection: existence and non-existence are equal for the world, so how does existence prevail? The answer is that non-existence is more original (aṣāla), so existence is actually outweighed (marjūḥ) relative to the world. If preponderance of an equal is impossible without a cause, then the emergence of existence which is outweighed is even more impossible without a cause. Therefore, a cause—the Creator—is necessary.

Key Terms
محدث
فاعل مختار
وجود
عدم
ترجيح
سبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the world could come into existence without a cause is possible, even if existence and non-existence are equal.
Correction: Sanusi argues that if existence and non-existence are equal, preponderance of existence without a cause is impossible. If non-existence is more original, existence is outweighed, making its occurrence even more impossible without a cause.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why must the originated world have an originator?
A) Because it is complex.
B) Because it cannot transition from non-existence to existence without a cause.
C) Because it could have always existed.
D) Because it is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The originated world's existence is contingent and requires a Creator, who freely chooses its time, measure, and attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that the world could not come from non-existence without a Creator. Have you truly allowed that realization to shape your daily actions? What would change if you lived constantly aware that your own existence is dependent on the free choice of Allah at every moment?
?
If you believe that the world could not exist without a cause, why do you often live as if your own decisions have no ultimate accountability? How does this argument demand that you submit to the Creator in every aspect of your life?
?
The passage argues that without the free agent, the world would remain in non-existence forever. When you act as if this world is self-sufficient, are you in fact committing an intellectual inconsistency? What is one concrete step you will take today to align your life with this truth?

The Proof of the World's Need for a Creator
Sanusi proves that the originated world requires a creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's argument that the world's origination proves it must have a creator, and how the necessity of a free agent is derived from the impossibility of a cause-free transition from non-existence to existence.

Core Idea
Origination demands an originator—nothing transitions from non-existence to existence without a cause.

Sanusi builds on the already established premise that the world is originated. Now he proves that this originated world necessarily requires a creator. His argument relies on the rational principle that any transition from non-existence to existence must have a cause, and without a free agent, the world would have remained in non-existence forever.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Get a feel for the logical flow of the argument.
Notice the key terms: حادث, محدث, فاعل مختار.
2
Identify the premise and conclusion
The premise is that the world is originated (حادث). The conclusion is that it must have an originator (محدث). Trace how Sanusi connects them.
3
Understand the argument for a free agent
Sanusi argues that without a free agent choosing when and how to create, the world would have stayed in non-existence. Why? Because all times and states are equally possible relative to its essence.
This shows the need for a selecting cause.
4
Examine the two views on existence and non-existence
Notice the two viewpoints: one says existence and non-existence are equal, the other says non-existence is more appropriate. Both lead to the same conclusion: a cause is needed to bring about existence.
Both reinforce the necessity of a creator.
5
Reflect on the final inference
Sanusi concludes that weighting existence without cause is impossible, even more so for a world that is preponderated (i.e., less likely) to be non-existent.
This seals the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في إقامة البرهان القاطع على وجوده تعالى و بيان احتياج العالم اليه جل وعز وإذا كانَ العالم حادثاً بعدما تقرَّرَ عدمُهُ ... فلا بدَّ لَهُ مِنْ محدث ؛ إذْ لا يُتصوَّرُ في العقل انتقالُهُ مِنَ العدم الذي كانَ عليه إلى الوجودِ الطارئ بلا سبب ، ولولا الفاعل المختارُ لوجوده فيما شاءَ مِنَ الأزمانِ على ما شاءَ مِنَ المقادير والصفاتِ .. لكان يجب أن يبقى على ما كانَ عليهِ مِنَ العدمِ أبد الآبادِ ؛ لاستواء المقادير والصفاتِ والأزمانِ بالنسبة إلى ذاته . وأما الوجود والعدم : فقيل : هما بالنسبة إلى ذاتِهِ سواءٌ ، فيستحيل أن يتربَّحَ الوجود المساوي الطارئ بلا سببٍ ، وقيل : العدمُ السابق أولى به ؛ لأصالته فيه ، وعدم افتقارِهِ إلى سببٍ ، وإذا كان ترجيح أحد المتساويين بلا سبب محالاً .. فاستحالة ترجیح الوجود المرجوح بالنسبة إلى العالم على هذا بلا سبب أحرى
Chapter: On establishing the decisive proof for His existence, may He be exalted, and explaining the world's need for Him, may He be glorified and exalted. And since the world is originated after its non-existence was established... it necessarily has an originator; for it is not conceivable in the intellect that it should transition from the non-existence it was upon to the incidental existence without a cause. And were it not for the free agent (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār) bringing it into existence whenever He wills from among times and in whatever manner He wills from among quantities and qualities... it would have to remain upon what it was upon of non-existence forever; because quantities, qualities, and times are equal with respect to its essence. As for existence and non-existence: it is said that they are equal with respect to its essence, so it is impossible that the equal existence which is incidental should outweigh without a cause. And it is said that the prior non-existence is more appropriate for it due to its being original in it and due to its not needing a cause. And if the weighting of one of two equals without a cause is impossible... then the impossibility of weighting the preponderated existence with respect to the world on this basis without a cause is more fitting.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of God based on the contingency of the world. Sanusi begins by stating the premise: the world is originated (ḥādith) after its non-existence was certain. From this, he argues that it necessarily has an originator (muḥdith), because it is rationally inconceivable for something to move from non-existence to existence without a cause. He then considers a hypothetical objection: if there were no free agent choosing to bring it into existence at a particular time with particular quantities and qualities, the world would have remained in non-existence forever, since all times and states are equally possible relative to its essence. Next, he discusses two views regarding the relation of existence and non-existence to the world's essence: one says they are equal, so a cause is needed to tip the balance towards existence; the other says non-existence is more appropriate because it is original and causeless. Both views lead to the conclusion that without a cause, existence cannot occur. Finally, he reinforces the argument: if weighting one of two equals without cause is impossible, then weighting the preponderated (i.e., less likely) existence without cause is even more impossible.

Key Terms
حادث (ḥādith)
محدث (muḥdith)
فاعل مختار (fāʿil mukhtār)
ترجيح (tarjīḥ)
الوجود والعدم (al-wujūd wa-l-ʿadam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the argument assumes the world's origination without proof, but Sanusi uses it as a premise already established in prior discussion.
Correction: The passage does not prove the world's origination; it builds on that premise to prove a creator.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the consequence if there were no free agent to bring the world into existence?
A) The world would have existed eternally.
B) The world would have remained in non-existence forever.
C) The world would have come into existence by itself.
D) The world would have existed but without qualities.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's decisive proof for God's existence rests on the logical necessity that an originated world cannot come into existence without a cause, which must be a free agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that without a free agent, the world would have remained non-existent forever. How does that truth confront your daily tendency to act as if your existence and blessings are self-made? What specific habit will you change to acknowledge that every moment you exist is because of Allah's free choice?
?
Sanusi says non-existence is more appropriate for the world. Yet you exist. Does that realization humble you or does it fade into theory? What will you do today to turn this truth into profound gratitude and surrender to your Creator?
?
The proof shows that the very fact you are reading this is impossible without a cause. When you ignore this dependence, you imply something false about reality. What is that falsehood, and how will you remind yourself hourly that your existence is a gift from the Free Agent?

Proof That the Creator is Eternal
Sanusi argues that the Creator must be eternal to avoid infinite regress or circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the originator of the world must be eternal, and why infinite regress (tasalsul) and circularity (dawr) are impossible.

Core Idea
If the Creator had a beginning, we would face an impossible chain of causes.

Sanusi begins by establishing a crucial attribute of the Creator: His eternity. He argues that if the originator of the universe had a beginning, we would be forced into one of two logical absurdities: an infinite regress of creators or a circular dependence. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage about the necessity of eternity once without analysing. Then read the translation.
Notice the concise style.
2
Identify the two absurdities
Find where Sanusi mentions tasalsul and dawr, and understand each definition.
Tasalsul is infinite regress; dawr is circularity.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Why are both considered impossible? Think about what they imply logically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يجبُ أنْ يكونَ مُحدِثُ العالم قديماً ؛ أي : لا أوَّليَّةَ لوجودِهِ ، وإلا لافتقر إلى مُحدِث ، ويلزم التسلسل فيؤدي إلى فراغ ما لا نهاية له ، أوِ الدَّورُ ، فيؤدي إلى تقدُّم الشيء على نفسِهِ ، وكلاهما مستحيل لا يُعقَلُ . ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ تعالى واجبَ البقاء ؛ أي : لا آخريَّةَ لوجوده ؛ إذ لو قبل أن يلحقه العدم لكان وجوده جائزاً لا واجباً ؛ لما عرفت أنَّ حقيقة الواجب : ما لا يتصوَّرُ في العقل عدمُهُ ، وهذا الوجود قد فُرِضَ أَنَّهُ يقبلُ العدمَ ، فيكون جائزاً ؛ إذ الجائز : ما يصح فيه الوجود والعدم ، والجائز يستحيلُ أنْ يقعَ بلا سبب ، فيحتاجُ إذاً هذا الوجود الجائز إلى سببٍ ، فيكونُ مُحدَثاً ، وقد قام البرهان على وجوب قدمِهِ تعالى . فإذاً ؛ فَرْضُ عدمِ وجوبِ البقاء في كلُّ ما قام البرهان على وجوب قدمِهِ . . تناقض لا يُعقَلُ
Then it is necessary that the originator of the world be eternal (qadīm), i.e., no beginning for His existence; otherwise He would need an originator, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul) resulting in an infinite void, or circularity (dawr) resulting in a thing preceding itself—both of which are impossible and inconceivable. And it is necessary that He, exalted, be necessary in persistence (wājib al-baqā'), i.e., no end for His existence; for if it were possible that non-existence should befall Him, then His existence would be contingent (jā'iz) not necessary (wājib); because you know that the reality of the necessary is that whose non-existence is inconceivable in the intellect. And this existence is supposed to admit non-existence, so it would be contingent; for the contingent is that in which existence and non-existence are both possible. And the contingent is impossible to occur without a cause, so this contingent existence would need a cause, and thus would be originated (muḥdath). Yet the proof has already established the necessity of His eternity. Therefore, supposing the non-necessity of persistence in anything for which the proof has established the necessity of its eternity is an inconceivable contradiction.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage contains two sequential proofs: first, that the originator of the world must be eternal (qadīm), and second, that He must be necessary in persistence (wājib al-baqā'). Sanusi begins by stating that the originator cannot have a beginning to His existence; if He did, He would need another originator, leading to either infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr). Both are impossible and rationally inconceivable. Then he argues that the originator must also be necessarily persistent, i.e., without end. If non-existence could possibly occur to Him, His existence would be contingent (jā'iz) rather than necessary (wājib). The necessary being is defined as that whose non-existence is inconceivable. A contingent existence cannot occur without a cause, so it would be originated, contradicting the already established proof of His eternity. Thus, supposing that something proven eternal could admit non-existence is a logical contradiction.

Key Terms
قديم (qadīm)
تسلسل (tasalsul)
دور (dawr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi say the originator of the world must be eternal?
A) Because the world is eternal.
B) To avoid infinite regress or circularity.
C) Because a creator must be greater than the creation.
D) Because the Qur'an says so.

Key Takeaway
The Creator must be eternal because any beginning would lead to an impossible chain of causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Creator had a beginning, He would need an originator. In your life, what created things do you rely on as if they were eternal? How does this argument expose the futility of depending on anything other than Allah?
?
The argument shows that infinite regress is impossible. Are there areas in your life where you make endless excuses or put off accountability, creating a 'regress' of responsibilities? What step can you take today to break that chain and turn sincerely to the Eternal?

Proof That the Creator is Necessarily Persistent
Sanusi proves that the Creator must be necessarily persistent, using the definitions of necessary and contingent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Creator must be necessarily persistent (wājib al-baqā') and why any possibility of non-existence would imply contingency.

Core Idea
If the Creator could cease to exist, He would be contingent, contradicting His eternity.

Having established the Creator's eternity (no beginning), Sanusi now proves His necessary persistence (no end). He argues that if non-existence were possible for the Creator, His existence would be contingent rather than necessary—which contradicts the preceding proof. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage on necessary persistence and its translation.
Note the definitions of wājib and jā'iz.
2
Understand the definitions
Define 'necessary' (wājib) as that whose non-existence is inconceivable, and 'contingent' (jā'iz) as that in which both existence and non-existence are possible.
3
Follow the proof chain
Assume non-existence possible → contingent → needs cause → originated → contradicts eternity.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يجبُ أنْ يكونَ مُحدِثُ العالم قديماً ؛ أي : لا أوَّليَّةَ لوجودِهِ ، وإلا لافتقر إلى مُحدِث ، ويلزم التسلسل فيؤدي إلى فراغ ما لا نهاية له ، أوِ الدَّورُ ، فيؤدي إلى تقدُّم الشيء على نفسِهِ ، وكلاهما مستحيل لا يُعقَلُ . ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ تعالى واجبَ البقاء ؛ أي : لا آخريَّةَ لوجوده ؛ إذ لو قبل أن يلحقه العدم لكان وجوده جائزاً لا واجباً ؛ لما عرفت أنَّ حقيقة الواجب : ما لا يتصوَّرُ في العقل عدمُهُ ، وهذا الوجود قد فُرِضَ أَنَّهُ يقبلُ العدمَ ، فيكون جائزاً ؛ إذ الجائز : ما يصح فيه الوجود والعدم ، والجائز يستحيلُ أنْ يقعَ بلا سبب ، فيحتاجُ إذاً هذا الوجود الجائز إلى سببٍ ، فيكونُ مُحدَثاً ، وقد قام البرهان على وجوب قدمِهِ تعالى . فإذاً ؛ فَرْضُ عدمِ وجوبِ البقاء في كلُّ ما قام البرهان على وجوب قدمِهِ . . تناقض لا يُعقَلُ
Then it is necessary that the originator of the world be eternal (qadīm), i.e., no beginning for His existence; otherwise He would need an originator, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul) resulting in an infinite void, or circularity (dawr) resulting in a thing preceding itself—both of which are impossible and inconceivable. And it is necessary that He, exalted, be necessary in persistence (wājib al-baqā'), i.e., no end for His existence; for if it were possible that non-existence should befall Him, then His existence would be contingent (jā'iz) not necessary (wājib); because you know that the reality of the necessary is that whose non-existence is inconceivable in the intellect. And this existence is supposed to admit non-existence, so it would be contingent; for the contingent is that in which existence and non-existence are both possible. And the contingent is impossible to occur without a cause, so this contingent existence would need a cause, and thus would be originated (muḥdath). Yet the proof has already established the necessity of His eternity. Therefore, supposing the non-necessity of persistence in anything for which the proof has established the necessity of its eternity is an inconceivable contradiction.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage contains two sequential proofs: first, that the originator of the world must be eternal (qadīm), and second, that He must be necessary in persistence (wājib al-baqā'). Sanusi begins by stating that the originator cannot have a beginning to His existence; if He did, He would need another originator, leading to either infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr). Both are impossible and rationally inconceivable. Then he argues that the originator must also be necessarily persistent, i.e., without end. If non-existence could possibly occur to Him, His existence would be contingent (jā'iz) rather than necessary (wājib). The necessary being is defined as that whose non-existence is inconceivable. A contingent existence cannot occur without a cause, so it would be originated, contradicting the already established proof of His eternity. Thus, supposing that something proven eternal could admit non-existence is a logical contradiction.

محدث (muḥdath)

Proof for God's Pre-eternity
Sanusi proves God's pre-eternity by eliminating regress and circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Creator must be pre-eternal (qadim) based on the impossibility of infinite regress (tasalsul) and circularity (dawr).

Core Idea
The First Cause cannot have a beginning; otherwise, an infinite chain or circle arises.

Sanusi begins by stating the conclusion that the Maker of the world must be pre-eternal. He then provides a concise rational proof: if the Creator had a beginning, He would need another creator, leading to an infinite regress or circularity, both of which are rationally impossible. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the first part of the source passage carefully. Note the key terms: qadim, tasalsul, dawr.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the two impossible consequences
Identify why tasalsul (infinite regress) and dawr (circularity) are impossible. The text states they are 'unintelligible' (la yu'qalu).
3
Connect the proof to the necessity of a First Cause
Recognize that the argument proves the Creator must be without beginning, because assuming a beginning leads to impossible outcomes.
This is a proof by contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
الدلیل علی وجوب قدمه جل وعز و وجوب بقائه
ثم يجبُ أنْ يكونَ مُحدِثُ العالم قديماً ؛ أي : لا أوَّليَّةَ لوجودِهِ ، وإلا لافتقر إلى مُحدِث ، ويلزم التسلسل فيؤدي إلى فراغ ما لا نهاية له ، أوِ الدَّورُ ، فيؤدي إلى تقدُّم الشيء على نفسِهِ ، وكلاهما مستحيل لا يُعقَلُ .
ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ تعالى واجبَ البقاء ؛ أي : لا آخريَّةَ لوجوده ؛ إذ لو قبل أن يلحقه العدم لكان وجوده جائزاً لا واجباً ؛ لما عرفت أنَّ حقيقة الواجب : ما لا يتصوَّرُ في العقل عدمُهُ ، وهذا الوجود قد فُرِضَ أَنَّهُ يقبلُ العدمَ ، فيكون جائزاً ؛ إذ الجائز : ما يصح فيه الوجود والعدم ، والجائز يستحيلُ أنْ يقعَ بلا سبب ، فيحتاجُ إذاً هذا الوجود الجائز إلى سببٍ ، فيكونُ مُحدَثاً ، وقد قام البرهان على وجوب قدمِهِ تعالى
فإذاً ؛ فَرْضُ عدمِ وجوبِ البقاء في كلُّ ما قام البرهان
على وجوب قدمِهِ . . تناقض لا يُعقَلُ
Chapter: The proof for the obligation of His pre-eternity (qidam), Majestic and Mighty, and the obligation of His persistence (baqa'). Then the maker of the world must be pre-eternal (qadim), i.e., no beginning for His existence; otherwise, He would need a maker, and there would be an infinite regress (tasalsul) leading to an infinite void, or a circle (dawr) leading to a thing's preceding itself, both of which are impossible and unintelligible. And it follows that the Exalted must be necessary of persistence (wajib al-baqa'), i.e., no end for His existence; for if He were susceptible to non-existence, His existence would be contingent (ja'iz) not necessary (wajib); because you already know that the reality of the necessary (wajib) is that whose non-existence is inconceivable in the mind. This existence has been assumed to accept non-existence, so it would be contingent; for the contingent is that in which existence and non-existence are both possible. The contingent cannot occur without a cause, so this contingent existence would need a cause, and thus would be originated (muhdath). Yet the proof has established the obligation of His pre-eternity. Therefore, the assumption of the non-obligation of persistence in anything for which the proof has established the obligation of its pre-eternity is a contradictory unintelligibility.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage contains two interconnected proofs: first for God's pre-eternity (qidam), then for His persistence (baqa'). The author begins by stating the conclusion: the maker of the world (al-muhdith) must be pre-eternal, meaning His existence has no beginning. He then provides the proof: if He had a beginning, He would need another maker, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul) of causes, which is impossible because it would imply an infinite series with no starting point, or else a circularity (dawr) where a thing precedes itself—both are absurd. Therefore, the First Cause must be without beginning. Next, the author proves that this Being must also be permanent (wajib al-baqa'), i.e., His existence has no end. The reasoning is that if He were susceptible to annihilation, His existence would be contingent (ja'iz), meaning it could possibly not exist. The definition of the necessary being (wajib) is that which cannot be conceived as non-existing. If He could cease, then His existence would be contingent, and every contingent requires a cause for its existence. That cause would then make Him originated, contradicting the established proof of His pre-eternity. Hence, assuming non-persistence for a being proven to be pre-eternal is a contradiction.

Key Terms
قديم (qadim)
التسلسل (tasalsul)
الدور (dawr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's pre-eternity means He is old, not that He has no beginning.
Correction: Pre-eternity (qidam) means existence without beginning, not just being old.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, which two impossibilities result if the Creator had a beginning?
A) Tasalsul and dawr
B) Taghayyur and huduth
C) Qidam and baqa
D) Fana' and 'adam

Key Takeaway
The Creator must be pre-eternal because assuming a beginning leads to an impossible infinite chain or circularity.

4 min
Proof for God's Persistence
Sanusi proves God's necessary persistence by showing the consequence of its denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be necessary of persistence (wajib al-baqa') based on the nature of the necessary being and the contingency of non-existence.

Core Idea
If God could cease to exist, He would be contingent and thus could not be the Pre-eternal Creator.

After establishing pre-eternity, Sanusi proves that God's existence must also have no end. He argues that if God were susceptible to annihilation, His existence would be contingent (ja'iz), requiring a cause, which would make Him originated—contradicting the proof of His pre-eternity. This lesson explores that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage for persistence
Read the second part of the source passage. Note the terms wajib al-baqa, ja'iz, and muhdath.
2
Understand the definitions of wajib and ja'iz
The text defines the necessary (wajib) as that whose non-existence is inconceivable. The contingent (ja'iz) accepts both existence and non-existence.
This distinction is crucial.
3
Follow the logical chain to the contradiction
Trace the argument: if not wajib al-baqa, then contingent; contingent needs a cause; that cause makes it originated; but pre-eternity is already proven. Thus the assumption leads to contradiction.

The reasoning is that if He were susceptible to annihilation, His existence would be contingent (ja'iz), meaning it could possibly not exist. The definition of the necessary being (wajib) is that which cannot be conceived as non-existing. If He could cease, then His existence would be contingent, and every contingent requires a cause for its existence. That cause would then make Him originated, contradicting the established proof of His pre-eternity. Hence, assuming non-persistence for a being proven to be pre-eternal is a contradiction.

Key Terms
واجب البقاء (wajib al-baqa)
الجائز (ja'iz)
المحدث (muhdath)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what would follow if God's existence could end?
A) He would be contingent
B) He would be pre-eternal
C) He would be a body
D) He would be unknowable

Key Takeaway
God must persist eternally because any possibility of non-existence would make Him contingent and contradict His pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's existence is absolutely necessary and permanent, while your existence is contingent and fleeting, what should be your deepest concern right now? How does that shift your focus today?
?
Since the proof shows that any possibility of God ceasing to exist would make Him contingent, and you know that only God is necessary, how does that affect your trust in His promises? What would it mean to live as if His persistence were uncertain?
?
If you truly internalized that you are a contingent being who exists only by God's will and that He alone is necessary and permanent, what one attachment or habit would you be compelled to change before the end of this day?

The Creator as Willing Agent: Refuting the Nature Objection
Sanusi proves the Creator is willing and not a nature, refuting the nature objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi proves that the Creator must be a willing agent rather than an impersonal nature or cause, and why the alternative leads to infinite regress.

Core Idea
The Creator's will is necessary to avoid the absurdity of an eternal preventer or infinite regress.

Sanusi now tackles a critical question: Is the Creator an impersonal cause or a willing agent? He anticipates an objection that the world's delayed existence could be explained by a nature requiring a condition. Through a devastating reductio, he shows that this explanation collapses into infinite regress, leaving only one rational conclusion: the Creator is a willing chooser. Let's trace his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal English translation to grasp the overall flow.
Pay attention to the conditional and the objection that follows.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two parts: a conditional statement about an eternal preventer, and a refutation of the objection that the Maker is a nature. Notice how the refutation builds on the conditional.
3
Understand the infinite regress argument
Focus on the refutation: if the world's existence depends on a temporal condition, then that condition itself must be explained, leading to either an eternal preventer (absurd) or another condition, causing infinite regress.
This shows the impossibility of an impersonal nature as an explanation.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The only way out of the infinite regress is that the Creator is a willing agent who freely chooses to create at a specific time without needing an external condition.
The text explicitly states: 'the Maker of the world is a willing chooser, not a cause nor a nature.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُوجَدَ العالم أبداً ؛ لأن مانعَهُ على هذا الفَرْضِ أَزلي ، فيستحيلُ عدمُهُ ؛ لما عرفْتَ أنَّ ما ثبت قدمُهُ استحال عدمه. وكذا الاعتراض ؛ بأن الصانع طبيعة ، وتأخر العالم عنها في الأزلِ لتوقف وجودِهِ على شرط لم يُوجَدُ في الأزل ، فلمَّا وُجِدَ الشرطُ فيما لا يزالُ وُجِدَ العالم عنِ الطبيعة حينَئِذٍ .. فاسد أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ الكلام في حدوثِ ذلكَ الشرطِ وتأخُرِهِ عنِ الأزلِ كالكلام في العالم، فيحتاج هو أيضاً إلى تقديرِ مانع أزلي ، فيلزم ألا يُوجَدَ شرطُ العالم أبداً ، فلا يُوجَدَ العالم مشروطه أبداً ، أو تقدير شرط آخر حادث ، فيُنقلُ الكلامُ إليه ، ويلزم التسلسل . فثبت بهذا : أَنَّ مُوجِدَ العالم مريد مختار ، لا علة ولا طبيعة .
The world would exist forever, because its preventer on this assumption is eternal, so its non-existence is impossible; because you have known that what is established as eternal, its non-existence is impossible. Likewise the objection that the Maker is a nature, and the world was temporally posterior to it in eternity because its existence depended on a condition that did not exist in eternity, then when the condition came to exist in the future, the world came to exist from the nature at that time — is also invalid; because the discussion regarding the occurrence of that condition and its temporal posteriority to eternity is like the discussion regarding the world, so it also needs the assumption of an eternal preventer, resulting that the condition of the world would never exist, so the world would not exist with its condition ever; or the assumption of another temporal condition, then the discussion is transferred to it, and infinite regress follows. Thus it is established by this: that the Maker of the world is a willing chooser, not a cause nor a nature.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by contradiction establishing that the Creator must be a willing agent, not a cause or nature. The author begins by supposing the opposite: if someone claims the world could never exist because an eternal preventer (مانع أزلي) blocks it, then the world would have to exist forever (since an eternal preventer cannot be removed, but the point is to show the absurdity of an eternal preventer leading to the world's non-existence). Actually, the first statement is a conditional: if there is an eternal preventer, the world would exist forever (because the preventer is eternal, the world's non-existence is impossible? This is confusing; the correct logic is: if the preventer is eternal, then the world would never exist because it is eternally prevented? Let me follow the text: 'يُوجَدَ العالم أبداً ؛ لأن مانعَهُ على هذا الفَرْضِ أَزلي' – This seems to say: The world would exist forever because its preventer on this assumption is eternal. That implies that if the preventer is eternal, then the world's existence is eternal? That doesn't make sense. Perhaps the meaning is: 'The world would not exist forever'? But the text has 'يُوجَدَ'. Possibly it is a typo for 'لا يُوجد'? But we must take it as given. The argument then says 'so its non-existence is impossible, because what is established as eternal cannot cease'. This is a statement about the impossibility of the world's non-existence if it were eternal. Then the objection: someone says the Maker is a nature and the world's existence is delayed until a condition arises. The author refutes this: the condition itself must then have an eternal preventer, leading to infinite regress. The conclusion is that the only valid position is that the Creator is a willing agent, not an impersonal cause or nature. The proof shows that the assumption of an eternal cause leads to absurdities, so the cause must be a free agent.

Key Terms

علة
طبيعة
مريد مختار
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some readers think this argument proves the world is eternal.
Correction: The argument actually proves the opposite: it shows that assuming an eternal preventer or an impersonal nature leads to contradictions, thereby establishing that the Creator must be a free agent who creates temporally.

Checkpoint

A) The world is eternal.
B) The Creator is a cause.
C) The Creator is a willing chooser.
D) The condition is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The only rational explanation for the world's existence is that its Maker is a willing agent, not an impersonal nature or cause.

?
The argument shows that the only alternative to infinite regress is a willing Creator. Are you living as if your own actions are guided by such a personal will, or do you drift through life as if driven by impersonal forces? What specific step will you take today to align your will with His?
