Why Multiple Gods Lead to Eternal Impotence
Sanusi argues that the impotence from multiple gods must be eternal, making the hypothesis self-contradictory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the assumption of multiple gods is self-contradictory because it requires an eternal impotence that cannot be incurred by the unchanging God.

Core Idea
The hypothesis of multiple gods self-destructs by requiring eternal impotence.

This passage builds on the earlier argument that the world's existence depends on a powerful God. Sanusi now examines the consequence of assuming multiple gods: each would be impotent due to lack of control. This impotence must be eternal, because God cannot acquire temporal attributes. This leads to a contradiction that refutes the entire hypothesis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
Pay attention to the key terms: القدرة (power), العجز (impotence), القديم (eternal), الحوادث (temporal events).
2
Identify the key premises
List the key premises: (1) The world depends on a powerful God. (2) Assuming multiple gods necessitates impotence for each. (3) This impotence must be eternal.
3
Follow the logical chain
Trace the argument: if power were eternal and impotence occurred later, that would be impossible because eternal power cannot cease. So the impotence must be eternal, but then God would never have had power, contradicting the original necessity.
Notice the conditional reasoning: 'if power eternal then impotence impossible'.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand why the assumption of multiple gods negates the very concept of God. The author says it is a case where 'its establishment leads to its negation'.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولتوقفه على وجودِ اللهِ قادر ، وقد لزمَ في هذا الفَرْضِ عجز الإلهِ ، وعجزه لا يكون إلا قديماً ؛ لاستحالةِ اتّصافِهِ بالحوادثِ ، ولو قُدِّرَ أَنَّ القدرة كانَتْ قديمةً ، ثم طراً عليها العجز .. لكانَ ذلكَ فَرْضاً مستحيلاً؛ لأنَّهُ يلزمُ حينَئِذٍ ألا تنعدم القدرة أبداً ، فلا يُوجَدَ العجزُ أبداً . فبانَ لكَ بهذا : أَنَّ فَرْضَ تعدُّدِ الإلهِ ينفي مطلق الإله الذي شهدَتْ بوجوبِ وجودِهِ معاينة مخلوقاتِهِ وبدائع مصنوعاتِهِ وبالجملة : فإثباتُ الإلهِ مُتعدّداً مِنْ بابِ ما أَدَّى ثبوتُهُ إلى نفيهِ فيكون منفيّاً ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق .
And because it (the world) depends on the existence of a powerful God, and in this assumption the impotence of God has become necessary, and His impotence is only eternal, due to the impossibility of His being qualified with temporal occurrences. And if it were assumed that power was eternal, and then impotence occurred to it, that would be an impossible assumption; because then it would necessarily follow that power would never cease, so impotence would never occur. So it has become clear to you by this that the assumption of multiple gods negates the absolute God whose necessary existence is witnessed by the contemplation of His creatures and the wonders of His handiworks. In summary: proving the existence of a multiplicity of gods is of the type where its establishment leads to its negation, so it is negated. And with God Most High is success.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of multiple gods by examining the nature of the impotence that would result. The author argues that the world depends on the existence of a powerful God, but the assumption of multiple gods necessitates impotence for each. This impotence must be eternal, because God cannot acquire temporal attributes (it is impossible for the eternal to change). If one were to suppose that God's power was eternal and then impotence occurred to it, that is impossible because an eternal power cannot be removed; it would exist forever, so impotence would never appear. Thus the hypothesis is self-contradictory. The author then concludes that the assumption of multiple gods negates the very concept of the absolute God whose existence is evident from creation. Therefore, affirming multiple gods is a case where affirming leads to negation, so it is negated.

Key Terms
القدرة
العجز
القديم
الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God could become impotent temporarily.
Correction: The author explains that change in the eternal is impossible, so any impotence would have to be eternal, not temporal.

Checkpoint
Why must the impotence that would result from multiple gods be eternal?
A) Because God is all-powerful.
B) Because it is impossible for the eternal to acquire temporal attributes.
C) Because the world depends on a powerful God.
D) Because power can end.

Key Takeaway
The hypothesis of multiple gods is self-refuting because it requires an eternal divine attribute to change, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that any being that is limited or subject to change cannot be God. Are there any 'gods' in your life — things you treat as ultimate authorities or sources of meaning — that are actually limited and changing? How does this logical proof challenge you to dethrone them?
?
The proof forces the conclusion that the true God must be absolutely powerful and eternal. When you face situations where you feel powerless or in need of control, how does this truth reshape your trust in the One who is never limited? What practical step can you take this week to rely more on His absolute power rather than your own?
?
Sanusi argues that the assumption of multiple gods is self-contradictory. In your own heart, do you sometimes live as if there are multiple sources of authority contradicting each other? How does this argument call you to submit fully to the one and only absolute authority in your life?

Denial of Any Created Causal Efficacy
Sanusi proves that no creature has any causal influence whatsoever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi denies any causal efficacy to creatures and how the argument rests on divine power and will.

Core Idea
No creature has any causal effect; all causality belongs to Allah alone.

Sanusi now extends the argument for divine unity to the realm of causality. Having established that only Allah is necessarily existent and all-powerful, he concludes that no creature can have any genuine causal influence. This passage is a direct application of tawḥīd al-afʿāl (unity of divine acts) and rejects any notion of secondary causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice the strong opening declaration and the logical structure that follows.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the key claim and its proof
Find the statement that no effect is from creatures. Then locate the reason given: that such would remove the effect from God's power and will, making the temporal overcome the eternal.
The proof is based on the impossibility of a contingent thing escaping God's control.
3
Examine the exhaustive list of negated effects
The author lists specific categories: motion/stillness, obedience/disobedience, and any effect at all, whether direct or generated.
This shows the conclusion applies to all types of actions and effects.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider how this teaching shapes one's understanding of divine sovereignty and human responsibility.
This is a core Ash'ari position on causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا فعل لغيرِهِ سبحانَهُ ولا مؤثَّرَ سواهُ وبهذا الدليل تعرفُ استحالةَ أنْ يكونَ لشيءٍ مِنَ العالم تأثير ألبتة في أثر ما ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ خروج ذلك الأثر عن قدرة مولانا جل وعزّ وإرادتِهِ ، وذلك يُوجِبُ أنْ يغلبَ الحادث القديم ، وهو محال فلا أثر إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ في حركة ولا سكون ، ولا طاعة ولا معصية، ولا في أثر ما على العموم ، لا مباشرةً ولا تولداً .
There is no action for other than Him, glorified is He, nor any effect besides Him. And by this proof you know the impossibility that anything in the world should have any effect at all in any effect whatsoever; because what follows from it is the exit of that effect from the power of our Master, glorified and exalted, and His will, and that necessitates that the temporal overcomes the eternal, which is impossible. So there is no effect, therefore, for the power of the creature in motion or stillness, nor in obedience or disobedience, nor in any effect at all, neither directly nor by generation.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage extends the preceding arguments to a further theological conclusion: the absolute denial of any causal efficacy in creatures. The author begins with a declarative statement: there is no action for other than God, and no effect besides Him. Then he says that through the proof (the previous argument about divine unity and power) one can know the impossibility of anything in the world having any effect whatsoever in producing any effect. The reason is that if a creature had an effect, that effect would be outside God's power and will. This would imply that a temporal (the effect) overcomes the eternal (God) — meaning that a contingent thing escapes the control of the necessary being, which is impossible. Therefore, the creature's power has absolutely no effect: neither in motion nor stillness, neither in acts of obedience nor disobedience, neither directly (mubāsharah) nor by generation (tawallud). This is a strong affirmation of divine causal exclusivity (tawḥīd al-afʿāl).

Key Terms
تأثير
القدرة
الإرادة
الحادث
القديم
مباشرة
تولداً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that creatures have independent causal power to produce effects, e.g., fire burns by its own nature.
Correction: Sanusi argues that any such causal influence would remove the effect from God's absolute control, which is impossible. Therefore, all effects are directly from Allah, not from creatures.

Checkpoint
What is the reason given for denying any effect of a creature's power?
A) Because creatures do not have free will.
B) Because it would imply that a temporal effect escapes God's power and will, making the temporal overcome the eternal.
C) Because God only acts directly.
D) Because the proof of mutual hindrance shows creatures are powerless.

Key Takeaway
All effects, whether direct or indirect, are solely from Allah; creatures have no causal efficacy whatsoever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that no creature has any effect, why do you still feel fear or hope in people’s actions? What does this reveal about the state of your tawhid?
?
When you perform an act of obedience, do you ever secretly credit your own strength or resolve? How does Sanusi’s proof challenge that feeling, and what must be your response when you sense that pride?
?
Think of a sin you blame on your environment or circumstances. How does the denial of any generated effect (tawallud) hold you accountable—not as a victim of causes but as one directly responsible before Allah?

The Impossibility of Multiple Gods
Sanusi proves the impossibility of multiple gods via a logical contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's logical proof that assuming multiple gods leads to a contradiction, thus negating the true God.

Core Idea
Multiple gods are impossible because the concept self-destructs.

Sanusi presents a concise but powerful proof (burhān) showing that the very idea of multiple gods is incoherent. Rather than simply stating a doctrine, he constructs a logical argument that begins with the assumption of a second god and shows that it necessarily leads to a contradiction. This passage demonstrates the rigor of kalām reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the logical flow from assumption to conclusion.
The Arabic uses compact, technical language typical of kalām.
2
Identify key terms
Find the terms for 'incapacity' (ʿajz), 'power' (qudra), 'eternal' (qadīm), and 'temporal event' (hādith). Understand their roles in the argument.
These terms are central to the proof.
3
Trace the argument steps
Follow the argument: assumption → necessity → impossibility → conclusion. Use the guided breakdown to see each logical step.
The proof is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on 'affirmation leads to negation'
Ponder the final statement: 'affirming a god as multiple is of the kind whose affirmation leads to its negation.' What does that imply about the concept of multiple gods?
This is the heart of the proof.
5
Connect to tawḥīd
Consider why this argument is foundational to Islamic monotheism. How does it reinforce the oneness of God?
It shows that tawḥīd is logically necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لتوقفه على وجودِ اللهِ قادر ، وقد لزمَ في هذا الفَرْضِ عجز الإلهِ ، وعجزه لا يكون إلا قديماً ؛ لاستحالةِ اتّصافِهِ بالحوادثِ ، ولو قُدِّرَ أَنَّ القدرة كانَتْ قديمةً ، ثم طرأ عليها العجز .. لكانَ ذلكَ فَرْضاً مستحيلاً ؛ لأنَّهُ يلزمُ حينَئِذٍ ألا تنعدم القدرة أبداً ، فلا يُوجَدَ العجزُ أبداً . فبانَ لكَ بهذا : أَنَّ فَرْضَ تعدُّدِ الإلهِ ينفي مطلق الإله الذي شهدَتْ بوجوبِ وجودِهِ معاينة مخلوقاتِهِ وبدائع مصنوعاتِهِ وبالجملة : فإثباتُ الإلهِ مُتعدّداً مِنْ بابِ ما أَدَّى ثبوتُهُ إلى نفيهِ فيكون منفيّاً ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق .
And because it depends on the existence of Allah being powerful, and in this assumption the incapacity of the god has necessarily followed, and his incapacity cannot be but eternal, due to the impossibility of his being described with temporal events. And if it were assumed that the power was eternal, then incapacity occurred upon it, that would be an impossible assumption, because then it would necessarily follow that power would never cease, so incapacity would never exist. So it has become clear to you by this: that the assumption of multiple gods negates the absolute god whose existence the observation of His creatures and the wonders of His creations have testified. In summary: affirming a god as multiple is of the kind whose affirmation leads to its negation, so it is negated. And by Allah Almighty lies success.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhān) demonstrating the impossibility of multiple gods. The argument begins by noting that if a second god were assumed, it would require him to be powerful. However, this leads to the necessary conclusion of his incapacity, which must be eternal because a god cannot acquire temporal attributes. If we suppose that his power was eternal and then incapacity occurred, that is impossible because eternal power cannot cease. Therefore, the assumption of multiple gods contradicts the existence of the true god attested by creation. In short, affirming multiple gods is self-refuting: its affirmation entails its negation, so it is negated.

Key Terms
تعدّد الآلهة
عجز
قدرة
قديم
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the argument assumes plural gods from the start and then rejects them based on doctrine.
Correction: The argument actually shows that the very concept of a second god is logically incoherent; it does not assume plural existence but proves impossibility through internal contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the outcome of assuming multiple gods?
A) It proves that multiple gods can exist
B) It leads to a contradiction that negates the true god
C) It shows that gods can have temporal attributes
D) It confirms the existence of two independent gods

Key Takeaway
The assumption of multiple gods is self-refuting because it forces a logical impossibility, thereby negating the very existence of the true God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any person, possession, or ambition in your life that you treat as if it has ultimate power over your happiness? How does this argument expose the falsehood of that 'god'? What step will you take today to dethrone it from your heart?
?
If the very concept of a second god is self-refuting, what does that say about any fear or hope you place in created beings as if they were ultimate? How can you realign your trust so that only Allah is your absolute reliance?
?
This proof shows that any rival to Allah is logically impossible. Yet you may still act as if something else holds ultimate control. What one concrete change in your daily habits would demonstrate that you truly believe no other god exists?

Knowing God: Obligation and the Role of Reason
Ibn Dihaq argues knowledge of God is obligatory and distinguishes necessary vs. acquired knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge of God's existence is rationally necessary and that further divine attributes require sound reflection on proofs.

Core Idea
Knowledge of God starts with reason, but faith deepens through reflection.

This passage from Ibn Dihaq's commentary establishes why we can know God. It argues that God obligates us to know Him, and such knowledge must be possible. The author then distinguishes between necessary knowledge of God's existence and acquired knowledge through reflection, setting the stage for proper theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the argument that knowledge of God is an obligation and thus possible.
Notice the use of the Quranic verse as support.
2
Identify the two types of knowledge
The passage distinguishes between knowledge of God's existence, which is innate to reason, and knowledge of further attributes, which requires reflection.
3
Understand the necessity of reflection
The author says that people differ on matters that require sound reflection on decisive proofs. This shows that reason alone is not enough for all knowledge of God.
4
Reflect on the obligation
Consider why impossible knowledge would be an unjust burden. This connects to divine justice.

ولنذكر هنا مِنْ « شرح ابنِ دهاق للإرشادِ » كلاماً رأيتُهُ متعلقاً بهذا الفصل، وهو حسن مفيد، وهذا نصه: ) قال أهلُ التحقيقِ : قد كُلِّفْنا بأن نعرف الله سبحانه، فلو كانَ العلمُ بهِ ممتنعاً .. لكان تكليفاً بما لا يُطاقُ، وهو غير واقع، ﴿لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٦]. والعلم بالله سبحانَهُ على وجهين : علم بوجودِهِ سبحانه، وذلك معلوم بضرورة العقلِ، فما رُبيَ في العقلاء مَنْ قالَ : ليس للعالم ربِّ يستند إليه ويصدر عنه وجودُ الخلق، ولكنهم اضطربوا في معلومات تُستدرَكُ بزائد على ضرورة العقلِ مِنَ النظرِ الصحيح في الأدلَّةِ القاطعة. وخُرَّجَ الغلط عند الجاهلينَ بالحقِّ على ثلاثِ طُرُقٍ (١): أحدها : في كيفيةِ صدورِ الخلْقِ عنه : فذهبَتِ الملحدةُ إلى أنَّ الخلْقَ صدرَ عنه صدورَ المعلولِ عن علَّتِهِ، وهذا يناقض حدوث المعلول، ويُفضي إلى قِدَمِهِ لقدم علتِهِ على أصلهم، أو إلى حدوثِ العلَّة لحدوث المعلولِ ! فمَنْ تبيَّنَ لَهُ وجوب حدوثِ العالم، ووجوبُ قِدَمِهِ تعالى .. علم أنَّ صدور العالَمِ عنِ اللهِ سبحانه صدور اختيار واقتدار. والطريق الثاني مِنْ وجوه الغلط : هو ما تخيَّلوهُ أنَّ موجوداً لا داخل العالم ولا خارجاً عنه مستحيل : فصاروا إلى القول بالتجسيم في حقّ الباري سبحانه وتعالى عن قول المغضوب عليهم علوّاً كبيراً
And let us mention here from 'The Commentary of Ibn Dihaq on al-Irshad' words I saw related to this chapter, and it is good and beneficial, and this is its text: 'The people of verification said: We have been obligated to know God the Exalted, and if knowledge of Him were impossible, it would be an obligation with what cannot be borne, and that does not occur. 'Allah does not charge a soul except with its capacity' [Al-Baqara 2:286]. And knowledge of God the Exalted is of two kinds: knowledge of His existence, and that is known by necessity of the intellect, for no rational person has been raised who said: the world has no Lord upon which it relies and from which the existence of creation issues. But they differed regarding matters that are grasped by something additional to necessity of the intellect, that is, sound reflection on decisive proofs. And error among the ignorant of the truth is traced back to three ways: One of them: concerning the manner of the issuance of creation from Him: the atheists held that creation issued from Him as the effect issues from its cause, and this contradicts the temporal origination of the effect, and leads to its eternity due to the eternity of its cause according to their principle, or to the temporal origination of the cause because of the temporal origination of the effect! So whoever has it clarified to him the necessity of the world's temporal origination and the necessity of His eternity knows that the world's issuance from God the Exalted is an issuance of choice and power. The second way of error: what they imagined: that a being neither inside the world nor outside it is impossible. So they ended up saying anthropomorphism regarding the Creator—Exalted and High is He above the saying of those who have incurred wrath, a great exaltation.'
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from Ibn Dihaq's commentary on al-Irshad, presenting a kalam argument for the possibility of knowing God and identifying sources of error. It begins by stating that we are commanded to know God; if such knowledge were impossible, it would be an impossible obligation, which God does not impose. Knowledge of God is twofold: necessary knowledge of His existence (innate to reason) and acquired knowledge of further attributes through sound reflection on decisive proofs. The author then states that error among the ignorant arises from three ways, but only two are given in this excerpt. The first way is misunderstanding the manner of creation: atheists (mulḥida) think creation issues from God as a necessary effect from a cause, which leads to either the effect being eternal (like its cause) or the cause being temporal (like its effect). The correct view is that creation is by choice (ikhtiyār) and power (iqtidār). The second way is the mistaken notion that a being cannot exist if it is neither inside nor outside the world, leading to anthropomorphism (tajsīm). The passage thus defends divine transcendence and the necessity of creation being by will, not necessary emanation.

Key Terms
علم بالله
ضرورة العقل
نظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that knowing God is impossible or that only faith without reason suffices.
Correction: The passage shows that knowledge of God is not only possible but obligatory, and it requires both innate reason and reflection.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Dihaq, what is the basis for knowledge of God's existence?
A) Sound reflection
B) Necessity of the intellect
C) Revelation alone
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of God's existence is rationally necessary; deeper knowledge requires sound reasoning on proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that knowledge of God's existence is inherent in your intellect. Yet have you ever consciously suppressed or ignored that innate awareness? What would change if you actively affirmed it today, not just as a fact but as the foundation of your life?
?
The passage calls for sound reflection on decisive proofs to know God deeper. When is the last time you truly reflected on a proof of God's attributes? Are you willing to set aside fifteen minutes this week to study one such proof with full attention?
?
You say you believe in God, but is your faith limited to the necessary knowledge that He exists, without progress? What specific attribute of God will you strive to understand more deeply this month, and what concrete step will you take to gain that knowledge?

Avoiding Error in Understanding God's Action and Nature
Ibn Dihaq explains two theological errors: necessary emanation and anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two common errors in theology: believing that creation is a necessary emanation from God, and anthropomorphizing God due to a misunderstanding of His relation to the world.

Core Idea
God creates by choice, not necessity; He is beyond inside and outside.

In this continuation, Ibn Dihaq identifies two ways people go wrong in understanding God. The first is thinking that creation issues from God necessarily, like an effect from a cause. The second is imagining that a being must be either inside or outside the world, leading to anthropomorphism. Both errors are corrected by proper understanding of divine transcendence and will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first error
Read about the atheists' view that creation is a necessary effect from God as a cause.
This is called 'necessary emanation'.
2
Understand the contradiction
If creation is necessary, either the world would be eternal (like God) or God would be temporal (like the world), both unacceptable.
3
The correct view
The world's issuance from God is by choice and power, preserving God's eternity and world's temporality.
4
Identify the second error
The mistaken notion that a being must be either inside or outside the world.
This leads to anthropomorphism (tajsīm).
5
The correct view
God is transcendent, not confined by space. He is neither inside nor outside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Two Types of Knowledge of God
Sanusi classifies knowledge of God into two types and introduces three errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between knowledge of God's existence (attained by necessary reason) and deeper knowledge requiring rational proof.

Core Idea
Knowing that God exists is universal; knowing what He is requires proof.

Sanusi begins by affirming that knowledge of God comes in two levels: a basic certainty shared by all rational people, and a deeper understanding that demands evidence. This foundational distinction sets the stage for critiquing those who err in their understanding of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening classification
Start by reading Sanusi's statement that knowledge of God is of two types. Notice how he immediately associates the first type with the necessity of reason.
The phrase 'ضرورة العقل' (necessity of reason) is a key term.
2
Identify the first type
The first type is knowledge of God's existence. Sanusi claims this is known by the necessity of reason, meaning no rational person genuinely denies it. Reflect on why he says 'ما رُبيَ في العقلاء' (no one raised among the rational) denies God.
3
Identify the second type
The second type is knowledge that requires additional reflection (النظر) and correct proofs (الأدلة القاطعة). This includes understanding God's attributes and actions beyond mere existence.
This sets up the need for kalam arguments.
4
Note the transition to errors
Sanusi then introduces the three ways of error among those ignorant of the truth. This bridges to the detailed critique in the following lessons.
The classification of errors shows why deeper knowledge is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعلم بالله سبحانَهُ على وجهين : علم بوجودِهِ سبحانه ، وذلك معلوم بضرورة العقلِ ، فما رُبيَ في العقلاء مَنْ قالَ : ليس للعالم ربِّ يستند إليه ويصدر عنه وجودُ الخلق ، ولكنهم اضطربوا في معلومات تُستدرَكُ بزائد على ضرورة العقلِ مِنَ النظرِ الصحيح في الأدلَّةِ القاطعة . وخُرَّجَ الغلط عند الجاهلينَ بالحقِّ على ثلاثِ طُرُقٍ : أحدها : في كيفيةِ صدورِ الخلْقِ عنه : فذهبَتِ الملحدةُ إلى أنَّ الخلْقَ صدرَ عنه صدورَ المعلولِ عن علَّتِهِ ، وهذا يناقض حدوث المعلول ، ويُفضي إلى قِدَمِهِ لقدم علتِهِ على أصلهم ، أو إلى حدوثِ العلَّة لحدوث المعلولِ ! فمَنْ تبيَّنَ لَهُ وجوب حدوثِ العالم ، ووجوبُ قِدَمِهِ تعالى .. علم أنَّ صدور العالَمِ عنِ اللهِ سبحانه صدور اختيار واقتدار . والطريق الثاني مِنْ وجوه الغلط : هو ما تخيَّلوهُ أنَّ موجوداً لا داخل العالم ولا خارجاً عنه مستحيل : فصاروا إلى القول بالتجسيم في حقّ الباري سبحانه وتعالى عن قول المغضوب عليهم علوّاً كبيراً . وربَّما تمسكوا بألفاظ لم يُحيطوا بمعانيها في اللغةِ ؛ مِنْ ذكرِ يَدٍ أو ساقٍ أو وَجْهِ أو عينٍ ، وتركوا العلم بحدوث العالَمِ مِنْ جهة الاستدلال ، واكتفوا بمُجرَّدِ القول بأنَّ العالَمَ فعلُ اللهِ تعالى ، ولم يتأملوا دليل الافتقار في العالم بأسره ، فورطَهم ذلك الحملُ على الظاهر في الجسميَّةِ والمكان والجهةِ . ولو تأملوا دليل الافتقار في العالم لعلموا أنَّ المتّصف بهذهِ الصفاتِ كفردٍ مِنْ أفراد العالم ، يجب حدوثه وعجزه كسائر العالم . ﴿ وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِى مَنْ أَسْرَفَ وَلَمْ يُؤْمِنُ بِشَايَاتِ رَبِّهِ ﴾ [طه : ١٢٧] . فهؤلاء عرفوا اللهَ مِنْ جهةِ القولِ ، لا مِنْ جهة الدليل ، وليس لهم حقيقة العلم بما يجبُ ويجوزُ ويستحيل عليهِ تعالى ، ﴿ وَمَا قَدَرُوا اللَّهَ حَقَّ قَدْرِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٩١] أي : ما عرفوا الله حق معرفتِهِ ، فما نفى عنهم المعرفة بالكليَّةِ ، ولكنَّهُ قالَ : ما عرفوا الله حقَّ معرفتِهِ ؛ أي : عرفوا وجوده ، ولم يعلموا الفَرْقَ بينَ وجودِهِ ووجود الحوادث بأدلة الحدوثِ في خَلْقِهِ . والطريقُ الثالثُ : الشَّرْكُ والعدد والحكم بأنَّ الآلهة كثيرة : وهذا الشِّرْكُ على أربعة أصنافٍ .
And knowledge of Allah, exalted is He, is of two types: knowledge of His existence, may He be exalted, and that is known by the necessity of reason; for no one has been raised among rational people who said: There is no Lord for the world to rely upon and from whom the existence of creation issues. But they disputed over matters that are grasped by what is additional to the necessity of reason, from correct consideration of decisive proofs. And the error among those ignorant of the truth is classified into three ways: The first: concerning the manner of the issuance of creation from Him: the atheists held that creation issued from Him as the effect issues from its cause, and this contradicts the temporality of the effect and leads to its eternity due to the eternity of its cause according to their principle, or to the temporality of the cause due to the temporality of the effect! So whoever has realized the necessity of the temporality of the world and the necessity of His eternity, may He be exalted, knows that the issuance of the world from Allah, exalted is He, is an issuance of choice and power. The second way of the aspects of error: is what they imagined that a being neither inside the world nor outside it is impossible: so they resorted to the claim of anthropomorphism concerning the Creator, may He be exalted, and He is far above the sayings of those who have incurred wrath, greatly exalted. And perhaps they clung to words whose meanings they did not comprehend in the language: such as mentioning a hand, or a leg, or a face, or an eye, and they abandoned knowledge of the temporality of the world through inference, and were content with merely saying that the world is the act of Allah, may He be exalted, and they did not reflect upon the proof of dependence in the entire world, so that literal interpretation led them into the pitfall of corporeality, place, and direction. And if they had reflected upon the proof of dependence in the world, they would have known that the one described with these attributes, as an individual of the world's individuals, must be temporal and incapable like the rest of the world. Thus do We recompense him who transgressed and did not believe in the signs of his Lord. [Taha: 127] So these people knew Allah in terms of speech, not in terms of proof, and they have no reality of knowledge of what is necessary, possible, and impossible for Him, may He be exalted. And they did not appraise Allah with true appraisal [Al-An'am: 91], meaning: they did not know Allah with true knowledge; so He did not negate knowledge from them entirely, but He said: they did not know Allah with true knowledge; meaning: they knew His existence, but they did not know the distinction between His existence and the existence of contingent things by the proofs of temporality in His creation. And the third way: polytheism, multiplicity, and the judgment that the gods are many: and this polytheism is of four types.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage enumerates and critiques errors in the knowledge of God. It begins by distinguishing two types: knowledge of God's existence (attained by necessary reason, as no rational person denies a Creator) and deeper knowledge requiring proof. Sanusi then classifies the errors of those ignorant of truth into three ways. The first error is that of atheists who view creation as necessary emanation from God, which implies either eternity of the world or temporality of God—both contradictions. The correct view is that creation issues from God by choice and power. The second error is anthropomorphism, stemming from the false assumption that a being cannot exist without location, leading to attributing bodily parts to God. They cling to scriptural terms (hand, face) without understanding their linguistic usage and neglect the proof of dependence that demonstrates creation's temporality. Had they reflected, they would see such attributes entail temporality and incapacity. The third error is polytheism and multiplicity of gods, which Sanusi notes has four types (though not fully enumerated here). Throughout, Sanusi emphasizes that proper knowledge of God requires inferential proof, not mere verbal acknowledgment.

Key Terms
علم بوجود
علم بالاستدلال
ضرورة العقل
نظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all knowledge of God is purely scriptural or mystical, but Sanusi emphasizes rational proof as essential for deep understanding.
Correction: Necessary reason gives basic existence; inferential reason provides detailed knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, which type of knowledge is known by the necessity of reason?
A) Knowledge of God's attributes
B) Knowledge of God's existence
C) Knowledge of the prophets
D) Knowledge of the afterlife

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of God has two levels: basic existence (self-evident) and detailed understanding (requires proof).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt a moment of doubt about God's existence? If so, does Sanusi's claim that it is self-evident challenge you to re-examine that doubt, or does it make you question whether you were truly using your intellect?
?
You already believe God exists—but do you actively seek to know His attributes through study and reflection, or have you stopped at 'He exists'? What would change in your worship if you knew Him more deeply?
?
When you meet someone who denies God, how do you respond? Do you assume they are irrational, or do you engage with their reasons? How might Sanusi's statement that 'no rational person truly denies a Creator' affect your approach to that conversation?

First Error: Atheists and Emanation
Sanusi critiques the atheistic view of necessary emanation and presents the correct view of voluntary creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the atheistic view that creation emanates necessarily from God is contradictory, and why the correct view is creation by choice.

Core Idea
Creation cannot be a necessary emanation; it must be voluntary.

Sanusi now details the first of three errors: the atheists' claim that the world proceeded from God as an effect from a cause. He argues this leads to absurd consequences and contrasts it with the correct understanding of voluntary creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the first error description
Begin with 'وخرج الغلط...' and read how Sanusi presents the error of the atheists (الملحدة). Note their claim: creation issues from God like a necessary effect.
The term 'الملحدة' refers to those who deviate from correct belief, often implying atheists or materialists.
2
Analyze the contradiction
Sanusi points out that if creation is a necessary effect of God, then either the effect is eternal (if cause is eternal) or the cause is temporal (if effect is temporal). Both are untenable. Work through this logic.
This is a classic kalam argument against emanationism.
3
Identify the correct view
Once one understands that the world is temporal (hadith) and God is eternal (qadim), the only coherent position is that creation occurs by choice and power (ikhtiyar wa iqtidar).
This affirms God's free will and omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعلم بالله سبحانَهُ على وجهين : علم بوجودِهِ سبحانه ، وذلك معلوم بضرورة العقلِ ، فما رُبيَ في العقلاء مَنْ قالَ : ليس للعالم ربِّ يستند إليه ويصدر عنه وجودُ الخلق ، ولكنهم اضطربوا في معلومات تُستدرَكُ بزائد على ضرورة العقلِ مِنَ النظرِ الصحيح في الأدلَّةِ القاطعة . وخُرَّجَ الغلط عند الجاهلينَ بالحقِّ على ثلاثِ طُرُقٍ : أحدها : في كيفيةِ صدورِ الخلْقِ عنه : فذهبَتِ الملحدةُ إلى أنَّ الخلْقَ صدرَ عنه صدورَ المعلولِ عن علَّتِهِ ، وهذا يناقض حدوث المعلول ، ويُفضي إلى قِدَمِهِ لقدم علتِهِ على أصلهم ، أو إلى حدوثِ العلَّة لحدوث المعلولِ ! فمَنْ تبيَّنَ لَهُ وجوب حدوثِ العالم ، ووجوبُ قِدَمِهِ تعالى .. علم أنَّ صدور العالَمِ عنِ اللهِ سبحانه صدور اختيار واقتدار . والطريق الثاني مِنْ وجوه الغلط : هو ما تخيَّلوهُ أنَّ موجوداً لا داخل العالم ولا خارجاً عنه مستحيل : فصاروا إلى القول بالتجسيم في حقّ الباري سبحانه وتعالى عن قول المغضوب عليهم علوّاً كبيراً . وربَّما تمسكوا بألفاظ لم يُحيطوا بمعانيها في اللغةِ ؛ مِنْ ذكرِ يَدٍ أو ساقٍ أو وَجْهِ أو عينٍ ، وتركوا العلم بحدوث العالَمِ مِنْ جهة الاستدلال ، واكتفوا بمُجرَّدِ القول بأنَّ العالَمَ فعلُ اللهِ تعالى ، ولم يتأملوا دليل الافتقار في العالم بأسره ، فورطَهم ذلك الحملُ على الظاهر في الجسميَّةِ والمكان والجهةِ . ولو تأملوا دليل الافتقار في العالم لعلموا أنَّ المتّصف بهذهِ الصفاتِ كفردٍ مِنْ أفراد العالم ، يجب حدوثه وعجزه كسائر العالم . ﴿ وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِى مَنْ أَسْرَفَ وَلَمْ يُؤْمِنُ بِشَايَاتِ رَبِّهِ ﴾ [طه : ١٢٧] . فهؤلاء عرفوا اللهَ مِنْ جهةِ القولِ ، لا مِنْ جهة الدليل ، وليس لهم حقيقة العلم بما يجبُ ويجوزُ ويستحيل عليهِ تعالى ، ﴿ وَمَا قَدَرُوا اللَّهَ حَقَّ قَدْرِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٩١] أي : ما عرفوا الله حق معرفتِهِ ، فما نفى عنهم المعرفة بالكليَّةِ ، ولكنَّهُ قالَ : ما عرفوا الله حقَّ معرفتِهِ ؛ أي : عرفوا وجوده ، ولم يعلموا الفَرْقَ بينَ وجودِهِ ووجود الحوادث بأدلة الحدوثِ في خَلْقِهِ . والطريقُ الثالثُ : الشَّرْكُ والعدد والحكم بأنَّ الآلهة كثيرة : وهذا الشِّرْكُ على أربعة أصنافٍ .
And knowledge of Allah, exalted is He, is of two types: knowledge of His existence, may He be exalted, and that is known by the necessity of reason; for no one has been raised among rational people who said: There is no Lord for the world to rely upon and from whom the existence of creation issues. But they disputed over matters that are grasped by what is additional to the necessity of reason, from correct consideration of decisive proofs. And the error among those ignorant of the truth is classified into three ways: The first: concerning the manner of the issuance of creation from Him: the atheists held that creation issued from Him as the effect issues from its cause, and this contradicts the temporality of the effect and leads to its eternity due to the eternity of its cause according to their principle, or to the temporality of the cause due to the temporality of the effect! So whoever has realized the necessity of the temporality of the world and the necessity of His eternity, may He be exalted, knows that the issuance of the world from Allah, exalted is He, is an issuance of choice and power. The second way of the aspects of error: is what they imagined that a being neither inside the world nor outside it is impossible: so they resorted to the claim of anthropomorphism concerning the Creator, may He be exalted, and He is far above the sayings of those who have incurred wrath, greatly exalted. And perhaps they clung to words whose meanings they did not comprehend in the language: such as mentioning a hand, or a leg, or a face, or an eye, and they abandoned knowledge of the temporality of the world through inference, and were content with merely saying that the world is the act of Allah, may He be exalted, and they did not reflect upon the proof of dependence in the entire world, so that literal interpretation led them into the pitfall of corporeality, place, and direction. And if they had reflected upon the proof of dependence in the world, they would have known that the one described with these attributes, as an individual of the world's individuals, must be temporal and incapable like the rest of the world. Thus do We recompense him who transgressed and did not believe in the signs of his Lord. [Taha: 127] So these people knew Allah in terms of speech, not in terms of proof, and they have no reality of knowledge of what is necessary, possible, and impossible for Him, may He be exalted. And they did not appraise Allah with true appraisal [Al-An'am: 91], meaning: they did not know Allah with true knowledge; so He did not negate knowledge from them entirely, but He said: they did not know Allah with true knowledge; meaning: they knew His existence, but they did not know the distinction between His existence and the existence of contingent things by the proofs of temporality in His creation. And the third way: polytheism, multiplicity, and the judgment that the gods are many: and this polytheism is of four types.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage enumerates and critiques errors in the knowledge of God. It begins by distinguishing two types: knowledge of God's existence (attained by necessary reason, as no rational person denies a Creator) and deeper knowledge requiring proof. Sanusi then classifies the errors of those ignorant of truth into three ways. The first error is that of atheists who view creation as necessary emanation from God, which implies either eternity of the world or temporality of God—both contradictions. The correct view is that creation issues from God by choice and power. The second error is anthropomorphism, stemming from the false assumption that a being cannot exist without location, leading to attributing bodily parts to God. They cling to scriptural terms (hand, face) without understanding their linguistic usage and neglect the proof of dependence that demonstrates creation's temporality. Had they reflected, they would see such attributes entail temporality and incapacity. The third error is polytheism and multiplicity of gods, which Sanusi notes has four types (though not fully enumerated here). Throughout, Sanusi emphasizes that proper knowledge of God requires inferential proof, not mere verbal acknowledgment.

صدور
معلول
علة
حدوث
قدم

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi say is the correct understanding of how the world issues from God?
A) As a necessary emanation
B) As an act of choice and power
C) As a natural process
D) As a mere illusion

Key Takeaway
The atheistic emanation model is self-contradictory; true creation is voluntary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's creation of you were a necessary emanation, would you feel any personal responsibility? How does knowing He chose to create you, freely and powerfully, change your sense of purpose?
?
Do you ever act as if God's commands are just natural consequences rather than choices from a free Lord? How can you remind yourself that every moment of existence is a voluntary gift?
?
When you sin, do you excuse yourself by thinking it was inevitable? How does the voluntary nature of God's creation and His power demand that you take full ownership of your actions?

Allah's Existence
intermediate

Second and Third Errors: Anthropomorphism and Polytheism
Sanusi critiques anthropomorphism and polytheism as errors rooted in ignorance of proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why anthropomorphism (attributing bodily parts to God) is an error and how the proof of dependence refutes it, and that polytheism is the third error.

Core Idea
Although God's hand, face, etc., are mentioned in scripture, they cannot be taken literally; the proof of dependence shows God is not like creation.

Sanusi now addresses two further errors: those who anthropomorphize God based on literal readings of scripture, and those who fall into polytheism. He emphasizes that proper inference from the proof of dependence (dalīl al-iftiqār) corrects these mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Read the second error
Start with 'والطريق الثاني...' and note how Sanusi describes the error of anthropomorphism. They claim a being cannot exist without being inside or outside the world, so they attribute location to God.
This is a philosophical argument against transcendent existence.
2
Understand the scriptural misuse
Sanusi criticizes them for clinging to literal words (hand, face, eye) without understanding their linguistic meanings or using the proof of dependence.
The proof of dependence shows all contingent things require a cause; God is not contingent.
3
Reflect on the proof of dependence
If they had used this proof, they would realize that attributing bodily features would make God temporal and incapable like other creatures.
This is a key kalam argument for tanzih (transcendence).
4
Note the third error: polytheism
Sanusi briefly mentions the third error as polytheism and multiplicity of gods, stating it has four types. This concludes the classification.
The passage does not elaborate on the four types, leaving them for further study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Prophets' Miracles: Beyond Magic and Trickery
Sanusi argues that prophets' miracles are genuine and distinct from magic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that prophets' miracles are genuine divine acts, distinct from any human trickery, as argued by Imam al-Sanusi.

Core Idea
Prophets' miracles are necessarily divine, not magic, because enemies could not expose any trickery.

How can we be certain that the extraordinary acts of prophets are truly from God and not mere magic or trickery? Imam al-Sanusi presents a compelling rational argument that the miracles of the prophets are beyond any human capability and definitively prove their truthfulness. This lesson will walk through the key points of this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi builds his argument step by step.
The passage begins with a rhetorical question to engage the reader.
2
Understand the core argument
Sanusi argues that prophets performed extraordinary acts that cannot be attained by any trick, magic, or deep knowledge. If they could be, it would be impossible for prophets alone to perform them throughout history.
The examples given include reviving the dead and splitting the sea.
3
Note the evidence from the Prophet's illiteracy
Sanusi cites Quran 29:48, which states that the Prophet Muhammad was not literate before revelation. This removes the possibility that the Quran came from human learning.
This is a specific proof for the Prophet's truthfulness.
4
Consider the role of enemies in verification
Sanusi points out that enemies and jealous people would eagerly search for any trick or flaw. Their failure to expose anything is strong evidence that the miracles are genuine.
Custom (ʿāda) makes it impossible for such a thing to remain hidden.
5
Arrive at the conclusion
The conclusion is that the truthfulness of all messengers is known by necessity (ḍarūra) to every person whom God grants success. This is not just inference but direct compelling knowledge.
The phrase 'by necessity' means it is self-evident to those who reflect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيف وقد أيَّدَهمُ الله تعالى بخوارقَ يُقطَعُ بِأَنَّهُ لا يُتوصَّلُ إليها بحيلة سحرٍ ولا غوص في طب ولا غيره ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وفلْقِ البحر أطواداً ، ونحو ذلكَ ممَّا لا يُتوصَّلُ إليهِ بالحِيَلِ ؛ إذْ لو كانَ يُتوصَّلُ إليه بالحِيَل لاستحال عادةً أن ينفردوا بذلك عن جميع أهل الأرض ؟! هذا ؛ وقد عُلِمَ ضرورةً أنَّهم كانوا في غاية البعدِ عن هذه العلوم وأربابها وأسبابها ، ﴿ وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُوا مِن قَبْلِهِ، مِن كِتَبٍ وَلَا تَنْظُمُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذَا لَّاَرْتابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ ﴾ [العنكبوت : 48] ، وهذا ممَّا أقرَّ به الموافق والمخالف هذا معَ أنَّ في نفوس الأعداء والحسدة ما يُحرِّكُ الدواعي إلى البحث والتفتيش ، والعادة تحيل أن تكون لهم نسبةٌ إلى شيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ إلا ويُعلَمُ ويُقرَّعونَ بهِ ، ويَشتهِرُ أمره حتى لا يخفى على أحدٍ وبالجملة : فصِدْقُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ معلوم على الضرورة لكلِّ موفَّقٍ
How, while God Almighty supported them with extraordinary things that are definitively known not to be attainable by any trick of magic, nor by deep knowledge of medicine or anything else—such as reviving the dead, splitting the sea into mountains, and the like that cannot be attained by tricks; for if it could be attained by tricks, it would be usually impossible that they alone should be distinguished in that from all the people of the earth? This, and it is known necessarily that they were in the utmost distance from these sciences, their masters, and their means. And you were not reciting before it any scripture, nor writing it with your right hand; then the falsifiers would have doubted. [al-Ankabut 48] And this is acknowledged by both the ally and the opponent. This, along with the fact that in the souls of enemies and the envious there is that which moves the motives to investigation and scrutiny, and custom makes it impossible that they should have any connection to anything of that without it being known and they being reproached with it, and its matter becoming famous so that it is hidden from no one. In summary: the truthfulness of the messengers—peace and blessings be upon them—is known necessarily to every one who is granted success.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof that the miracles (mu'jizat) performed by the prophets are genuinely divine and cannot be imitated by magic or human skill. The author begins by stating that God supported the prophets with extraordinary events that are definitively known to be unattainable by any trick of magic or deep knowledge in fields like medicine. Examples include reviving the dead and parting the sea. The argument is that if such acts could be achieved by trickery, it would be impossible for them to be exclusively performed by prophets throughout history. Additionally, it is a matter of necessary knowledge that the prophets were completely removed from the sciences that might produce such things. The author then cites Qur'an 29:48, which confirms that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was not literate, further removing any suspicion of human origin. The proof continues by noting that both allies and opponents acknowledge this. Furthermore, the enemies of the prophets, driven by jealousy and hatred, would eagerly investigate and expose any trickery; the fact that they could not find any evidence of fraud is itself proof of authenticity. The conclusion is that the truthfulness of all messengers is known by necessity (darura) to every person whom God grants success. This is not a mere inference but a direct, compelling knowledge.

Key Terms
خوارق
معجزة
ضرورة
صِدْق الرُّسُل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that prophets' miracles could be mere magic or advanced human trickery.
Correction: Sanusi argues that miracles are definitively beyond any trick, as shown by the uniqueness of prophets in performing them, their ignorance of such arts, and the inability of enemies to expose any fraud.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what prevents the possibility that prophets' miracles could be mere tricks?
A) The miracles are simple and easy to perform
B) The enemies would have exposed any trickery, and the prophets were ignorant of such sciences
C) The miracles were performed only in secret
D) The prophets were magicians themselves

Key Takeaway
The truthfulness of the messengers is known necessarily through the unique, inimitable nature of their miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading that the truthfulness of the messengers is known necessarily to every successful person, ask yourself: Do you know it as a necessity, or is it just a belief you hold? What might be blocking you from that certainty? Examine your heart and commit to removing any doubt by studying the proofs more deeply.
?
The passage says enemies and the envious scrutinized the prophets but could find no fault. Is your own scrutiny of the prophets and their message led by a desire for truth or by something else? If you have ever doubted, have you honestly investigated the evidence as the enemies did? Make a firm intention today to search for truth with sincerity, not with a preconceived rejection.
?
The Qur'anic verse about the unlettered Prophet Muhammad (29:48) is presented as a proof that the Quran is not from human sources. Does this remove any lingering doubt you have about the divine origin of the Quran? If not, what more do you need to be convinced? Be honest with yourself and take a step towards certainty by reflecting on the miracle of the Quran in your own life.
